Read the passage in <A> and examine the teaching procedure in <B>.Then follow the directions. [3 points]AProcessing instruction, a type of focus-on-form instruction, is basedon the assumption that when processing input, L2 learners havedifficulty in attending to form and meaning at the same time due toworking memory limitations. Not surprisingly, they tend to give priorityto meaning and tend not to notice details of form. Processing instructionuses several principles to explain what learners attend to in the inputand why. Below are some of these principles.The Lexical Preference Principle: In (1), both -es and boy conveythe same information, ‘the third person singular’. Yet, learners prefer tofocus on the lexical item, boy, to arrive at meaning, and often ignorethe grammatical item, -es, while processing the sentence.(1) The boy studies in the library, not at home.The First Noun Principle: Learners tend to process the first noun orpronoun they encounter in a sentence as the agent of action. For example,they may misinterpret (2) as “Jack collected the data for the project.”(2) Jack \et Joe collect the data for the project.The Event Possibilities Principle: Event possibilities refer to thelikelihood of one noun being the agent of action as opposed to another.Since it is more likely in the real world that a dog would bite a manthan the other way around, learners would likely misinterpret (3) as “Thedog bit the farmer.”(3) The dog was bitten by the farmer.In processing instruction, teachers provide students with structuredinput activities, taking into consideration the principles above. In astructured input activity, students are forced to attend to form in orderto comprehend a sentence.of“Guideline for Pre-service Teachers |Teaching Procedure1. Explicit ExplanationExplain how a past tense sentence is constructed in English. Theninform students of why they tend not to notice the past tense marker-ed and thus misinterpret past tense sentences.2. Structured Input ActivityHave students read six sentences and decide whether they describean activity that was done in the past or usually happens in thepresent. Then, check the answers together.(1(2(3(4(5(6They watched television at night.They watch television at night.I walk to school on Mondays.I walked to school on Mondays.We played soccer on weekends.We play soccer on weekends.디디디디디니다티디티디디Identify the principle in <A> that the teaching procedure in <B> focuseson. Then explain how the structured input activity in <B> helps studentscorrectly process the target form for meaning.| Answer | The structured input activity in <B> is based on the Lexical PreferencePrinciple. In this activity, students are exposed to the pairs of sentencesin the activity, in which each pair has the same lexical meaning butdifferent tenses. Thus, it requires them to focus on the lexical meaningfirst and the form (the past tense marker -ed) second. In other words,through a form-meaning relationship in this activity, they distinguishthe present from the past tense by noticing the past tense marker ‘ed,’resulting in naturally processing it.a] 6.야 om 7 eae Be? | 에대한형식을 e 익히고보다꼼꼼한 directions} “ae 분석에ae 하도록 한다. 따라서기본강좌를 익히고, 실제수업」대한 do | 터를분석하도록하는원서강독까지진행한 후, 해당자료나학습상대한특징이나문제점등을이끌어내 “ae 표현해보고해결책을제시하는글을써보s서져근교실황도{fl02. Learners respond to thestimulus Cinguistic input), and reinforcement strengthens (habituates) theTesponse; they imitate and repeat the language that they hear, and whenthey. are ‘reinforced for that response, learning occurs. The implication is that“practice makes perfect.”p sey wat nto \, Sruct u helfsyva구조주의관점에따르면언어란개별적항목으로분해될수 있으며, 이런개별언어들은과학적으로기술ᆞ대조될수 있으며, 각각의개별적항목이통합된것이바로언어 이다.Build-up 영어교육론 12.행동주의에따른교실지도(1) Teaching method : Audiolingual method행동주의는프로그램학습과통제된 연습, HES pattern drillo] 사용된청화식교수WH (Audiolingual Method)2] 토대가 되었다. 따라서교사는학습환경을조성하고모방과 연습, 강화스케줄을마련하여자신이의도하는방식으로학습자가반응하도록반복적 이고, 기계적으로언어학습을하여해당언어를습관화시ᄏ문형을반복연슴시켜 JOA 한 다음, 필요에 파라, 습관적으로그문형을사용할수호그나huco도aN3© USS 통해새로나온어휘와구조들을제시 한다.(3) 대화에 uel 문형을 7|4# repetition, backward build—up, chain, substitution,transformation, question and answerS 수행 한다,@ 문법은주어진예문에서얻어지며 , 명시적문법규칙들은제시되지 않는다.© 문화정보는대화의문맥또는교사에의해제시된 다.© 읽기와쓰기 BRE 이전에연습했던 Gero] 기초한 다.Behaviorism is the theory that human beings learn new behaviors througha stimulus and response cycle. In language learning it holds that language islearned mimicry and memorization of form which leads to habit formation.It suggests that the goal of instruction is to replace bad habits(errors) withgood ones(grammatical utterances). This theory resulted in the creationand extensive use of drills for teaching foreign languages. This method ofteaching relied heavily on the use of memorization of set dialogues andextensive repetition and drilling. It was developed in the 1950s as a methodfor teaching foreign languages to military personnel very quickly. However,when used in the public schools and universities throughout the world, itfell short of producing competence users of foreign languages. Why is that?Language production is not based on predictable, set dialogues. Languageuse can be unpredictable and it will vary depending on the contexts in which( Spent an€ovs) CPlagwatics, semantics >is produced.Chapter 01 언어습득및학습유형 75Chaptereee(2) 기계적학습t그]ou+lo새로운학습자료를기존의인지구조와의상호작용없이개별적이고독립적으로단기기억에저장하므로반복적인연습이없으면장기기억화되기가 어렵다.Rote learning involves the mental storage of items having little or noassociation with existing cognitive structure.fuin(3) The Audio—lingual MethodO|A] 강조되는언어분야및언어기능(Structuie )@ 언어구조들이다른분야에비해강조된 다.@ 구조교수 요목, 어휘도대화내에서문맥에근거하여제시된 다.@ 구두 - 청취의기능이관심의대상 이다. “^ 160(L&S)=e Further readingAudiolingualismAudiolingualism2 행동주의에입각해 habit formationz} stimulus/response associationOl| 의해언어습득이이루어진다고 본다.In the audiolingual method, structures of the target language werecarefully ordered And dialogues repeated in an attempt to develop correcthabits of speaking. Sentences in substitution activities, mim-mem (mimicand memorize), and other drills were usually related only syntactically(‘I go to the store,” “You go to the store,” “He goes to the store”),and they generally had nothing to do with actual events or narrative.Sometimes, however, these sentences did resemble real communicationin that the situational scenarios to be memorized included greetingsand idiomatic expressions. Rules were presented but often not formallyexplained, and activities such as minimal pairs (seat-sit, yellow-Jell-O,etc.) were commonly used in an effort to overcome the negative transfer .(interference) of first language (L1) sounds. Listening and speaking skillstook precedence over reading and writing skills. However, in most of theapplications, there was very little use of creative language, and a greatdeal of attention was paid to correct pronunciation. Often practice sessionstook place in fully equipped language laboratories (Richard-Amato, 2002).26 Build-up 영어교육론 1. 행동주의에대한비판행동주의에따르면아동들은강화에의해언어를학습하 지만, 한번도강화를받지못한언어적 BSE 나타낸다. 따라서어린이의언어는외부적인환경에의해형성되기보다는자신의언어체계를창조적으로발달시켜가는 Alt} (Littlewood, 198").Imitation and reinforcement have a much smaller role to play in childlanguage. For example, children often produce forms that they never heardtheir parents or other adults say (‘I goed” or “two foots”). Thus, imitationof adult speech cannot completely account for the way children producelanguage: “The child’s language is simply too strange” (McLaughlin 1984,p.15). Furthermore, parents rarely correct their children’s grammatical errorsbut respond instead to the message content (Brown and Hanlon 1970;Brown 1973). If ungrammatical forms are thus positively rewarded (or atleast ignored), how then do children eventually eliminate them? A behavioristview of language, which would predict the need for both imitation and_negative feedback in the form of overt corrections, does not seem to explainthe way in which children learn (Hadley, 2001).1,개념1) 인지주으ia+)xo,lr( 오2,피 ×In인지주의에따르면어린이는언어규칙을이용하여언어를구사 sj장치 (1. ᄉ 1); Language Acquisition Device)S 가지고태어나기에단기간에언어습득이가능하며 , 이러한언어습득장치는모든인간에게보편적인것으로서무한한양의창의적발화를도와 준다.20|0/8t4(Meaningful learning)( schewa )인간의언어학습에는체계성이 있어, 새로운항목을학습했을경우기존인지구조안에의미하게연관시켜포섭 한다.C 609 어 ) C subsumption )」filaoJoiNI“JChapter 01 언어습득및uidetine for Pre-service Teachers eS |Chapter(3)28Learning takes place in the human organism through a meaningful processof relating new events or items to already existing cognitive concepts orpropositions handing new items on existing cognitive pegs. Meaningfullearning is the process of relating and anchoring new material to relevantestablished entities in cognitive structure. As new material enters thecognitive field, it interacts with and is appropriately subsumed under, amore inclusive conceptual system. (24-7IS"%?é^ 놀CfChapter2) 구성주의자신에게주어지는지식을수동적으로받아들이는것이 아니라, 사회적상호작용을통해서능농적으로지식을스스로재구성한 다.Constructivism is a theory of learning that claims that individuals activelyconstruct knowledge, rather than passively receiving it. They do this byfiltering and organizing their experience so as to match their existingknowledge(or mental representations) of the world. If there is a mismatchbetween their experience and their existing mental representations, theyrestructure the latter to accommodate the new information. According to thisview, different individuals who are exposed to the same experiences willeach construct a different and unique reality.. 구성주의에따른교실지도SFO] 및구성주의에따른언어학습은언어의본질적인요소인언어의기능을중시하므로, 실제교실지도에서언어의기능학습이라는대명제로언어학습을시도 하였다.그런데 dole) 기능이란상황에따라달라지므로효과적인 devisees 위해실제언어사용을토대로한상호작용학습이출현하게 되었다.(1) Schematic knowledgeLanguage learners make use of their knowledge of the world to help themcomprehend texts. Research has shown that learners possess schemata, i.e.mental structures that organize their knowledge of the world which theydraw on in interpreting what they heard or read.(2) Individual difference30If some people are better at some thins than others — better at analysing,for example — this would indicate that there are differences in the waysindividual brains work. Personalization creates better classroom dynamics.This is because groups are more likely to form and bond if the individualsin them know more about one another. And the mental and emotional effortthat is involved in finding personal associations with a language item islikely to make them more memorable. Finally, lessons are likely to be moreinteresting, and enhance more motivation rather than the characters in coursebooks.(4) Learner—centered instructionLearner-centered instruction aims to give learners more say/in areas thatare traditionally considered the domain of the teacher/y providing learnerswith greater autonomy. This term applies to curricular as well as to specifictechniques. It can be contrasted with teacher-centered, and has receivedvarious recent interpretations. Learner-centered instruction includes:@ techniques that focus on or account for learners’ needs, styles, and goals.@ techniques that give some control to the student (group work or strategytraining, for example).® curricula that include the consultation and input of students and that donot presuppose objectives in advance.(4) techniques that allow for student creativity and innovation.® techniques that enhance a student’s sense of competence and self-worth.(5) Whole language approach] 제생활 (681 life) 안에서의언어사용은개별적인언어 능력, S 듣기, 말하기, 읽기,쓰기등이독립적으로사용되는것이 아니다. 따라서통합적인측면에서실제효과어학습을이루어야적절한의사소통능력을배양할수 있다. 이러한목적을실현하기위하여 Whole Language Approach 측면에서통합수업 모형, 즉듣기와말하기수계등이현재교실수업에서실현되고있는 것이다.r& oe 제32 Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3)Integrated skills activities can provide a model for integrating skills in arealistic way and is especially useful at a post-elementary level. [ 기입혐 ]34Long followed up his work on organizational pattern in the classroomwith an investigation of the characteristics of small group tasks mostlikely to facilitate acquisition. In a study reported in 1981, he foundthat two way tasks stimulated significantly more modified interactionthan one way tasks. Similarly, Doughty and Pica (1986) found thatrequired information exchange tasks generated significantly moremodified interaction than tasks in which the exchange of informationwas optional. The term modified interaction refers to those instancesduring an interaction when the speaker alters the form in which his orher language is encoded in order to make it more (1) | ᅵ Suchmodification may be prompted by lack of comprehension on the part ofthe (20) =.ROME (1), compehensivde^ inputBuild-up 영어교육론 |deline for Pre-service Teachers 3 3) |02) Read the passage and fill in the blank with suitable words. (delivered in an environment whereoF WN =」 ol AD 00 으4 > of itSi?students are “off the defensive”)Chapter 02 제 2 언어습득모형 43Chapter@ Affective Filter Hypothesis정의적여과막이란학습자가지닌학습에대한정의적인변인이학습에장애가되는방향으로작용하는것을 말하며, 낮은동기와낮은 자신감, 높은불안있다. 따라서성공적인언어습득을위해서는이러한정의적여과막ᄋThe affective filter is “a mental block” that prevents acquires from fullyutilizing the comprehensible input they receive for language acquisition.A number of affective variables such as motivation, self-esteem andlow anxiety can play a facilitative role in successful second languageacquisition. Low motivation, low self-esteem, and high anxiety, on theother hand, can work to raise an affective filter. In other words, when thefilter is up it hinders language acquisition.(3) Natural Order HypothesisrirAd법og문법체계는예측가능한순서대로습득 되는데, 이러한자연적인발달구조의복잡성이나의도적인문법지도와는별개로발달 한다.The natural order hypothesis states that the acquisition of grammatical서는structures in a second language follows a predictable natural order. Thisorders is independent of instructional sequences or even_of the complexity ofthe structures to be acquired. Thus, when the learners are engaged in naturalcommunication tasks they will manifest the standard order.(4) Monitor Hypothesis44모니터란학습자의발화에서오류를감지하여잘못된표현을개선하거나수정장치 이다. Krasheno] 따르면학습된언어적지식 (168101 knowledge)o] 학습언어출력을감시하는모니터역할을수행 한다.Learning has only one function, and that is as a monitor or editor to하는자의make changes in the form of our_utterance, after it has been produced bythe acquired system. Acquisition initiates the speaker’s utterances and isof the acquired. system before or after the utterance is actually written orspoken.Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers Ss) J한다.lok>ra4Alas0rzJf웨ca- 2ofolt. 씬dorokrhBYrh=m2©2.2[에ho. 언어출력의정확성과형태에초점을맞춰야 한다.The focus must be on form and not meaning.3, 출력된언어에적용된규칙을알아야 한다.The user must know the rule.2. 시사점Krashen suggests that there are certain implications for classroom practice iflanguage instruction is to be consistent with his theory. Among these are:(@® The main function of the classroom may be to provide comprehensible inputin an environment conducive to a low affective filter 01.6., high motivation,low anxiety).@ The classroom is most useful for beginners, who cannot easily utilize theinformal environment for input. That is, it is useful for foreign languagestudents who do not have input sources outside of class or for thosewhose competence is so low that they are unable to understand thelanguage of the outside world.@ The requirements for optimal input are that it be @) comprehensible,() interesting and relevant, © not grammatically sequenced, @ provided insufficient quantity to supply i+, and © delivered in an_environment wherestudents are “off the defensive.”® Error correction should be minimal in the classroom; it is of some limiteduse when the goal is learning, but of no use when the goal is acquisition.Error correction raises the affective filter and should, therefore, not beused in free conversation or when acquisition is likely to take place.® Students should never be required to produce speech in the second languageunless they are ready to do so. Speaking fluency cannot be taught, but“emerges” naturally in time with enough comprehensible input (Hadley, 2001).Ly NAChapter 02 제 2 언어습특모형 445Chapter3. Krashen 모형에대한비판@ Acquisition—learning HypothesisOl| 대한비판 : 학습된언어적지식은 une 통해습득으로이어질수있으며실제학습과습득의상호작용에의해발화로연결된 다.In second language learning, learning and acquisition can both bebeneficial. Declarative Knowledge & Procedural KnowledgeDeclarative knowledge is concerned with knowledge “aboutsomething” (knowing that). With regard to language, it relates to suchaspects of language as word knowledge (collocation, pronunciation,meaning). This information is relatively accessible to consciousawareness. Procedural knowledge relates to cognitive skills (knowhow). Using language is thought to involve procedural knowledgeand, unlike declarative knowledge, is relatively inaccessible.2. Noticing HypothesisAccording to noticing hypothesis, nothing is learned unless it hasbeen noticed. Noticing does not itself result in acquisition, but it isthe essential starting point. Noticing refers to becoming aware of alanguage feature in the input.52 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers & ==a@® :~ Further reading |선천주의모델과인지주의 GAS 통한외국어학습에있어형식적인교수 (10013! instruction) 역할의 3 가지입장1. Krashen2] 모형 ( 비접촉적 입장, non-interface position)Krashen2 언어형태에초점을둔형식적인외국어학습에서얻어진학습된 AAS 습득으로이어지지않는다고하면서습득된지식과학습된지식은완전히분리된지식서로관련이없다고 본다. Krashenoll 의하면외국어교실의가치는문법있는것이아니라이해가능한교사의언어 ((68 아 6『 talk)Oll 있으며외국어교수가언어형태보다의사소통에 AAS 둘때진정한의미의습득이일어난다는 것이다.The non-interface position has been advanced most strongly byKrashen (1982). Krashen, it will be recalled, identifies two types oflinguistic knowledge in SLA. “Acquisition” occurs automatically whenthe learner engages in natural communication where the focus is onmeaning and where there is comprehensible input. “Learning” occursas a result of formal study where the learner is focused on the formalproperties of the L2. “Acquired” knowledge consists of subconsciousL2 rules which the learner can call upon automatically; “learnt”knowledge consists of metalingual knowledge which can only beused to monitor output generated by means of “acquired” knowledge.Krashen argues that the two knowledge types are entirely separate_andunrelated. In particular he disputes the view that “learnt” knowledge isconverted into “acquired” knowledge. This is the non-interface position.Krashen advances a number of reasons for the separateness of “acquired”and “learnt” knowledge;@ There are plenty of case of “acquisition” where no “learning” hasoccurred. These are widely reported in studies of naturalistic SLA.(2) There are cases where “learning” has taken place but where it hasfailed to become “acquisition”. Krashen refers to the case of “P”(Krashen and Pon, 1975), who had “learnt” rules like the third personsingular “-s”, but was unable to use them in casual conversationbecause she had not yet “acquired” them.Chapter 02 제 2 언어습득모형 453Chapter제 2 언어습득모형(03) Even the best “learners” can master only a small subset of thegrammatical rules of the L2. This is because most of the rules arefar too difficult for the average “learner” to follow. Krashen pointsout that it often takes a linguist years to describe successfully rulesthat are easily “acquired”.2. McLaughlin7} Bialystok2| 모형 ( 접촉적 입장, interface position)o학습자가비록다양한종류의외국어지식을갖고 있지만, 이지식은서로분리된것이아니라연습을통하여어느한지식이다른쪽으로 ype 수있다고 본다.BialystokOl) 의하면명시적 AALS ASS 통하여습득과유사한암시적 (묵시적) 지식으로전환될수있다고 하였다. 또한요실에서외국어를배운학습자는자연적인외국어학습자를능가한다고 보았는데, 그이유는 첫째, 직접적으로는 ' 흡입 (00186) 이가능한교실 SHA (hol?)때문이며, 둘째, 간접적으로는연습을통하여명시적지식을자동화시킬수있기때문이 다.Bialystok also develops a model of SLA based on two types ofknowledge which can interact. She calls these knowledge types“implicit” and “explicit”, but it is clear from her description of themthat they correspond fairly closely to Krashen’s “acquired/learnt”types. Bialystok suggests that practice serves as the mechanism bywhich explicit knowledge turns into implicit knowledge. Thus implicitknowledge can be built up in two different ways; (1) the primarymeans is “unconscious acquisition”, and (2) the secondary means isthrough the automatizing of explicit knowledge by practice. Oneway, then, in which “acquired” and “learnt” may be connected is interms of automaticity. This is a view developed by McLaughlin (1978)in his attack on Krashen’s non-interface position. McLaughlin refersto Schneider and Shriffin’s (1977) distinction between “controlled”and “automatic” processing. “Controlled” processing requires activeattention, so that only a limited number of features can be controlledat a time without interference occurring. “Automatic” processingtakes place without active control or attention. The important pointis that “automatic” processes are learned following the earlier use of“controlled processes”. Thus SLA entails going from the controlledto the automatic mode of operation. It is, therefore, not necessary topresuppose two unconnected knowledge types such as the “acquired/learnt” distinction.54 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers = 3) |Pus 5input ProcessingInout Processing 이론에따르면학습자들은언어적정보의표면적인 형태, 문법구조보다정보의내용과그의미를먼저인식하고인지적으로처리 한다. 《1/656496 7 Ferm)The input processing theory assumes that learners have preferences forsemantic processing over morphological processing. That is learners processinput for meaning before they process it for form, so that, for example, theyprocess content words in the input before anything else, prefer to extractsemantic information from lexical items rather than grammatical items (suchas inflections),and prefer to process meaningful morphology rather than non-meaningful morphology.103| 구성주의모형 |1. 구성주의모형elton 에라(1) L0009 의 Interaction hypothesis 조기입장 — Importance of comprehensible input언어습득에기여하는 ANS AER (interaction)2] 기능을강조한 다, 언어의습득은상호작용5과정중에발생하는의미의 SBA Negotiation of 2068201208) 과 주정: 된상호작용 (\//001860interaction)o] 의하여언어적입력이보다이해가능해진다는 것이다. 1008 의 InteractionHypothesis: 현재의사소통중심언어수업 (2601011411081146 Language '1'6801208) 을기반으로하는교실수업을뒷받침 한다.According to Interaction Hypothesis, conversational interaction is anessential for second language acquisition. (context based product)(2) Long2| Interaction hypothesis 후기입장 — Importance of corrective feedback56의사소통가설의후기입장은의사소통과정에서일어나는교정적인 Bw (corrective[66068009 의중요성이강조 되었다. 대화참여자들은 ' 의미의 BPs] 과정을통해의사소통의어려움을해결할뿐아니라언어를발달시킬수있는기회를얻는다고본다.In Long’s (1996) revised version of the Interaction Hypothesis, moreemphasis is placed on the importance of corrective feedback duringinteraction. When communication is difficult, interlocutors must “negotiatefor meaning”, and this negotiation is seen as the opportunity for languagedevelopment. Merrill Swain (1985) extended this thinking when sheproposed “the comprehensible output hypothesis”. She observed that it iswhen learners must produce language/that their interlocutor can understandthat they ai are most likely to see the limi it of their second language abilitySeeand the teed to find better ways to express their meaning. The demands ofproducing comprehensible output, she hypothesized, “push” learners aheadin their development.Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3 ᅵ2. Vygotsky2] Sociocultural TheoryLong 7} 마찬가지로언어습득에서의상호작용의역할을중시하면서상호작용이언어습득에끼치는영향을근접발달영역 (1116 Zone of Proximal 126?010001601) 과Al (Scaffolding) 등의개념으로설명한 다.A key concept in Sociocultural Theory is that interaction not onlyfacilitates language learning but is a causative force in acquisition; further,all of learning is seen as essentially a social process which is grounded insociocultural settings.(1) 근접발달영역 (16 Zone of Proximal Development)학습자가혼자서는해결할수없지만자신보다뛰어난동료혹은성인의도움으로해결할수있는잠재적인학습영역을뜻한 다.lrThe distance between the actual developmental level as determinedby independent problem solving and the level of potential developmentas determined through problem solving under adult guidance or in_collaboration with more capable peers.What this means is that learning@ Scaffolding Hypothesis4]A|(Scaffolding= 보다뛰어난학습자혹은성인이의사소동과정에서제공하는도움을뜻한 다. 이는학습자에게언어적입력을보다이해가능하게만들어의사소롱의문제를해결할뿐만아니라 ZPD 내에서의언어발달을촉진하는기등을 한다.One way in which others help the learner in language developmentwithin the ZPD is through scaffolding. This includes the verticalconstructions, in which experts commonly provide learners with chunks oftalk that the learners can then use to express concepts which are beyondtheir independent means. More generally, the metaphor of scaffoldingrefers to verbal guidance which an expert provides to help a learnerperform any specific task, or the verbal collaboration of peers to performa task which would be too difficult for any one of them individually.60 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers & , __7)ly In the ClassroomCollaborative Learning (Scaffolding)The following constructed dialogue illustrates the negotiation of meaningin a typical one-to-one communication. She argued thatamong other functions, output is a significant way to test out hypothesesabout the target language. Swain (1995) suggests that “pushed output”(1.6., Output that is accurate and sociolinguistically appropriate) may beChapter 02 제 2 언어습득모형 ^ 61Chapternecessary for learners to achieve higher levels of linguistic and sociolinguistic competence. According to Swain (1995), pushed output facilitatesacquisitions, as it (1) helps learners to discover that there is a gap betweenwhat they want to say and what they are able 10 527, (2) provides a way forlearners to try out new rules and modify them accordingly, and (3) helpslearners to actively reflect on what they know about the target language _system. According to Ellis (1997), the use of linguistic knowledge underreal conditions of communication. In other words, learners “need to see forthemselves what has gone wrong, in the operating conditions under whichthey went wrong”A : I go cinema.B : You what?A: I went to the cinema.In the Example, A is led to reformulate her initial utterance, producinga more grammatical version of it, as a result of B’s clarification request.Thus, this kind of exchange provides an opportunity for what Swainhas called pushed output, i€. output that reflects what learners canproduce when they are pushed to ‘use the target language accuratelyand concisely.ate Further readingPositive evidence vs Negative evidence1, Positive evidence : well-formed sentences to which learners are exposed _학습자에게제공되는목표언어의정확하고올바른입력@ The most obviously necessary requirement for learning(2) It can be authentic or modified. Where did you go?S : I go to IFC mall.Recasts are complex discourse structures that have been said to containpositive evidence (a model of the correct form), and negative feedback(since the correct form is juxtaposed with the non-target like form) inan environment where the positive evidence is enhanced (because ofjuxtaposition). If learners do not selectively attend to and recognize thenegative feedback contained in recasts, then the documented contributionof recasts to learning might be attributed to the positive evidencethey contain, or to the enhanced salience of the positive evidence.. Negative evidence : information that is provided to learners concerningthe incorrectness of an utterance학습자의발화의부정확성에대하여언급하는정보 FSS 말한다.@ pre-emptive : occurring before an actual error — as in a classroom context오류가실제로발생하기이전에제공되는오류에대한 SHS 가리킨다.© reactive : 실제일어난오류에대한교정적정보 로서, 명시적인형태와묵시적인형태가있다AA ᆞExplicit evidence is an overt correction. Where did you go?S : Iwent to IFC mall.* Clarification requests : The teacher uses phrases such as “Pardonme?” or “I don’t understand.” Or, the teacher asks another question,Chapter 02 제 2 언어습득모형 63Chapter64제 2 언어습득모형such as “What do you mean by x?” This request signals to thestudents that there was some kind of error, or something was notclear in their language use, and invites them to reformulate theirutterance. Teachers normally make use of clarification requestswhen students make meaning related errors while the focus is oncommunication.T : How old are you?S : thirteenT : Pardon me?S > Thirty.* Explicit correction : The teacher directly tells a student what themistake was and provides the correct answer. For example, shemight say, “oh, you mean,.,,” or “you should say,,.” or “the correctform of this verb form is,,.,” An alternative of this strategy is toask a peer student, other than the one who committed the error, toprovide the correct answer.T : Where did you go after class yesterday?S : Igo home.T : Go is not the correct past tense form. The CAH claimed that theprincipal barrier to second language acquisition is the interference of thefirst language system with the second language system. The goal of CA isto isolate what needs to be learned and what does not need to be learnedin a second language learning situation.@ 단계description .—» selection -——» contrast —-» © predictionNDAI31®wmtrong version : 오류가발생하기전두언어의차이점을기술하여학습의어려움을예측, 오류의출현을막고자 한다.One could predict the patterns that will cause difficulty in learning,and those that will not cause difficulty, by comparing systematically thelanguage to be learned with the native language.76 Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) 1(2) Weak version실제언어학습후발생하는학습자의 OFS 토대로두언어오류의근원을밝히고자 한다.대조분석하여cucuUnlike the strong version, it begins with the comparison after the actualproblem occurred. That is, based on the actual and recurring difficultiesexhibited in the learner’s performance, it attempts to account for thedifferences between the native language and the target language.3. 대조분석의한계점언어학습과정에서발생하는오류의근원을모국어로만한정 하였다. 즉학습자의오류는모국어의간섭이외의것에서발생한다는점을간과 하였다.The most of the errors learners make in 12 cannot be traced to thedifferences between L1 and L2. In addition, regardless of the features of thestudents’ first languages, they appear to go through similar variable stages inthe second language. As a result of the finding that man aspects of learners’language could not be explained by the CAH, a number of researchers beganto take a different approach to analysing learners’ errors. This approach,which developed during the 1970s, became known as ‘error analysis’ andinvolved detailed description and analysis of the kinds or errors secondlanguage learners make.Pus | .Positive Transfer vs Negative TransferTransfer means that the transfer of elements acquired in L1 to the target L2.ᆞ Positive(facilitating) Transfer : when the same structure is appropriate in bothlanguages.« NegativeGinterference) Transfer : when the L1 structure is used in appropriatelyin the L2.Chapter 03 언어분석및중간언어 -- / /ChapterAly In the ClassroomContrastive analysis is based on behaviorism. It considers L1 to be mainlyin interference to the mastery of L2. In order to become proficient in L2,the habits of L1 need to be “broken” before the habits of L2 can becomefirmly established. Thus, audiolingualism its most well-known manifestation,presented us with mim-mem drills and practice with minimal pairs suchas chew and shoe (for Spanish speakers), glass and grass (for Koreanspeakers), and dialogues to be memorized so that students could avoiderrors in the new language and take on its proper forms.Students who learn English as a foreign language already have a deepknowledge of at least one other language, and where L1 and Englishcome into contact with each other there are often confusions whichprovoke errors in a learner’s use of English. This can be at the level ofsounds: Korean, for example, does not have a phonemic distinctionbetween /r/ and /l/ and Korean speakers may well say lice when theymean rice. It can be at the level of grammar where a student’s firstlanguage has a subtly different system: our students often have troublewith article usage and the present perfect because Korean doesn’t havesuch a form. Thus, in order to solve the problems, the teacher shouldprovide students with meaningful minimal pairs practice at the level ofsounds and grammar.78 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers1031IzFlJor띠 >Ra}r221. 학습자언어 ( 중간 언어, Interlanguage)L creative System ( shyt 다름)(1) 7H중간언어란학습자가목표어를습득하는과정중발생하는것으로모국어와목표어의중간에있는불완전한언어체계를 말한다.Interlanguage means an intermediate system located somewhere betweenthe learner’s native language and the target language, but governed by itsown unique and coherent internalized rule system that rarely becomes totallycongruent with the system of the second language.(2) 중간언어의특징(1) Learner language is systematic.중간언어는나름의일정한체계를 가진다. 그러나 BE 학습자가똑같은중간언어체계를갖는것은 아니다.At any particular stage of development, the IL is governed by ruleswhich constitute the learner’s internal grammar.Ex, 부정문에관한규칙에대해서문두에 Nott Not& 사용하는경우No speak English. Continue ©C) Green (+) CY) erAffective cognitiveFeedback FeedbackChapter 03 언어분석및중간언어 - 87Chapter88aly In the ClassroomFeedback@ Explicit Correction : A teacher provides the correct form, he or sheclearly indicates that what the student had said was incorrect, forexample, “Oh, you mean....” “You should say....”@) Recasts : A teacher reformulates all or part of a student’s utternance,minus the error. Recasts are generally implicit.(3) Clarification requests : A teacher indicate to students either that theirutterance has been misunderstood or that the utterance ‘is ill-formedin some way and that a repetition or a reformulation is required. Aclarification request includes phrases such as “Pardon me.”, “What doyou mean by...?” and so on.Metalinguistic feedback contains comments, information, or questionsrelated to the well-formedness of the student’s utterance, withoutexplicitly providing the correct form.&£x, Can you find your error?It’s a masculine.Is it feminine: (00446)©) Elicitation : Teachers use to directly elicit the correct form from thestudent using questions (How do we say X in French?), incompletesentences (It’s a....) and asking students to reformulate their utterance.© Repetition: A teacher repeat the student’s erroneous utterance. Inmost cases, teachers adjust their intonation so as to highlight theerror. Question types@ Display question : a question which is not a real question but which servesto elicit language practice.Ex, Is this a book?Yes, it’s a book.Chapter 03 언어분석및중간언어 95Chapter@) Referential question : a question which asks for information which is notknown to the teacher, such as What do you think about animal rights?In a language classroom, “display” questions were determinant in teacher’sinteraction with learners, and that “referential” questions were more conduciveto the production of lenghtier and more complex responses by learners. Ithas been suggested that one way to make classes more communicative is forteachers to use fewer display questions and more referential questions.|? Example |T : Last week we were reading “Kee Knock Stan” [title ofa story]. What is “KeeKnock Stan”, Hyunsoo?: Lcannot understand.: Yes.: What do you think the postman at the post office would do?(그 think I would divide it if the letters are to Hong Kong or other places.: Yes, I think that’s a sensible way, right? Good.YN ye nBoth questions asked by the teacher are “what” questions, but the first oneis a “display” question which has only one correct answer, hence “closed”.The second is a “referential” question with no pre-determined answer, hence“open”.2. Effective questioning효과적인질문기법은학슴자가교사의질문에대답할수있도록유도하는것으로질문에대한대답을이끌어내지못할경우교사는즉각자신의질문을학습자의수준에맞춰수정해야할 것이다.Language teachers in questioning are usually to get their students to engagewith the language material actively through speech ;so an effective questioningtechnique is one that elicits fairly prompt, motivated, relevant and full responses.if, on the other hand, their questions result in long silences, or are answered byonly the strongest students, or obviously bore the class, or consistently elicitonly very brief or unsuccessful answers, then there is probably somethingwrong. Thus, when teachers fail to elicit any response from the learners, theyoften need to modify their questions. There are a number of modification96 Build-up 영어교육론 LGuideline for Pre-service Teachersdevices used by teachers, including syntactic modifications (such as making thetopic salient and decomposing complex structures) and semantic modificationssuch as paraphrasing difficult words and disambiguation.For example, in a language classroom, the teacher read out a sentencedescribing a dog. She said “So that’s a very good descriptive sentence. It tells youexactly what the dog look like. Can you picture the dog?”The teacher realizedthat the use of the word “picture” might be a bit beyond the pupils’ ability level.Therefore, she modified the question to “If I were to ask you to draw the dog,would you be able to draw the dog?” As a result of her lexical modification, thestudents immediately responded in chorus by saying “yes, yes”.3. Cohesive 06006( 결합장치 ) 가없어도하나의주제 (6010) 하에문장들이논리적관계를이루고있다면응집력이있는텍스트 (00166text)7} 될수 있다.If a text is coherent, it makes sense. The coherent sentences are relatedto each other, and relate in our background knowledge of the world. Thefollowing text is coherent:Ex. We want you to be delighted with this facility. If there is a fault with thetoilet please call extn 1071 on the nearest white courtesy phone.The language and organization of the text are appropriate, especiallywhen we know that the text was written to be read in an airport restroom.Moreover, the two sentences of the text have a logical relation.(2) Cohesion(#et#4)결합력이란글의요소들이연관되어있는정도로주로단대명사, 지시대명사의사용등에의해결정된 다. Ashes 응결합력이있다고해서반드시응집력있는 16 파라고할수는 없다.에If a text is cohesive, its elements are connected. Cohesion is the use ofgrammatical and lexical means to achieve connected text, either spokenor written. Unlike coherence, which different readers or listeners mayexperience to varying degrees, cohesion is a stable property of text. Andwhile cohesion may help make a text coherent, it cannot guarantee it.Cohesion[ ... |Grammatical Lexical|Reference Substitution Ellipsis(endophoric) ©| |Repetition Synonyms Superordinates .- General wordsChapter 03 언어분석및중간언어 _ 9901. FI learnersto profit more from decontextualized analytic approaches and formalinstruction.Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teacher s=e Further readingFl vs FDA field independent (FD style enables you to distinguish parts froma whole, to concentrate on something Cike reading a book in a noisytrain station), to analyze separate variables without the contaminationof neighboring variables. On the other hand, too much FI may resultin cognitive “tunnel vision”: you 566 only the parts and not. theirrelationship to the whole. “You can’t see the forest for the trees,” as the‘saying goes, Seen in this light, development of a field dependent (FD)style has positive effects: you perceive the whole picture, the largerview, the general configuration of a problem or idea or event. It is clear,then, that both FI and FD are necessary for most of the cognitive andeffective problems we face.ᆞ like to analyze information into its | « like to deal with information structurescomponent parts and _ distinguish as wholesthe essential from the inessential ᆞ are sociable and work well in groups¢ prefer to find solutions to problems | +* have difficulty discerning a figurefor themselves apart from the field* are more particularistic and analytic.) * are more global and holistic in pro-cessing new information2) 좌되 (! 라 brain) vs 우뇌 (101 brain)© 좌뇌 : 논리적, 분석적사고및수사학적 , 신형직 : 징보처리에능한학습유형 으로,10)(63) 우뇌 : 시각, 촉각, 청각적이미지로 지각, 기억하여 통합적, 전체적, 정서적정보나내oOHu 0Nt‘0aeaa2bya422 1Je,AUoot0[ ᄋ00|anJu :bs( 으+re,Chapter 04 학습자변인 109ChapterMost of the time, when we are learning something we use both the leftand right brain. Use both sides and your brain will staybalanced.(3) 모호함에대한 Z=(ambiguity tolerance)외국어학습시모국어와다른언어규칙이나문화에대해관용적인태도를취해야보다성공적으로제 2 언어를습득할수 있다.It entails an ability to deal with ambiguous new stimuli without frustrationand without appeals to authority. Successful language necessitates toleranceof such ambiguities, at least for interim periods or stages, during which timeambiguous items are given a chance to become resolved.(4) $21 &(reflectivity) vs SS (impulsivity)C19 ca \ Systunret¢ )SUS reflective) 학습자 : 체계적이고논리적인사고에의해학습하기때문에문제"결에 시간이다소걸리지만충동형보다 OFS 적게발생시킨 다.Cinturhe ) Covel)@ SSAimpulsive) 학습자 : 신속하며직관적으로과제를처리 하며, 문맥을통한유추가뛰어나기때문에오류가발생하더라도유추를통해과제를처리할수 있다.(8) Reflective learners :* prefer doing things more slowly and moving ahead in logical steps.ei* like to thing quite a lot before making a decision.* need to be certain of the right answer before trying it out.* usually make fewer comprehension error in reading,(6) Impulsive learners :* like to do things fast.* enjoy making guesses and are willing to be wrong sometimes.ᆞ are often good at guessing the meanings of words and sentences.‘are fast readers since they often ignore words that they don’timmediate understand.110 Build-up ozS= 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers=e Further readingReflectivity vs ImpulsivityOne important learning style is speed, that is, how slow or fastsomeone is. If you prefer doing things more slowly, your style isreflective. If you like to do things fast, your style is impulsive. Reflectivepeople usually like to think quite a lot before making a decision. Theyneed to be certain of the right answer before trying it out. They slowlymove ahead in logical steps. They're usually slower readers, who want tomake sure that they understand what they're reading before continuing.Consequently, they usually make fewer comprehension errors in reading.On the other hand, impulsive learners are faster thinkers. They usuallyenjoy making guesses. They are also willing to be wrong sometimes.They are usually fast readers since they often ignore words or phrasesthat they don’t immediately understand and just continue reading. Whilethey make more errors in reading, they are often good at guessing themeanings of words and sentences. Both styles have advantages anddisadvantages.More accurate speaking ᆞ More willing to speak in classAdvantages | * More accurate reading + Faster readingᆞ Think carefully before acting | » Better in timed testsᆞ Wait too long to speak * Less accurate in speakingDisdvantages | * Read more slowly ᆞ Less accurate in reading* Slower in timed tests * Act without thinking enough® 시각형 (16481 style) vs 청각형 (34010 style)Visual learners tend to prefer reading studying chart, drawings, and othergraphic information, while auditory learners prefer listening to lecturesand audiotapes.Chapter 04 학습자변인 1.11ChapterFour Learning StylesDirect means of processing information; people:orientated; spontaneous; imaginative; emotional; dislikesAnalytical learningstyleFocuses on specific problems and proceeds by meansof hypothetical-deductive reasoning; abjecPorientated;independent; dislikes failure; prefers logical, didacticpresentation.learning styleFairly independent; highly adaptable and flexible;responsive to facts that do not fit; prefers s6cial learningand a communicative approach; enjoys taking decisions.Authority-orientated,learning styleReliant on other people; needs teacher’s directions andexplanations; likes a structured learning environment;intolerant of facts that do not fit; prefers a sequentialprogression; dislikes discovery learning.이| ly In the ClassroomRead about two different students in the same English class.<Student 1>112 Build-up 영어교육론 lDiscovering Students’ Learning StylesMaria is eighteen years old and wants to go to a university in theUnited States. Self Confidence (Self-esteem)자신과자신의능력에대한자신감은제 2 언어습득에서중요한요소로방어기제(Inhibition), 71@4>(Risk—taking), 긴장감 (&470346[9) 등과영향을주고 받는다.Self-esteem refers to the degree to which individuals fee confident andbelieve themselves to be significant people. Closely related to the notionof self-esteem is the concept of inhibition and language ego, risk-taking,anxiety, empathy and so on.(Grlence® C4 [osing fore |(1) Inhibition & Language ego학습자는외국어학습시자신감과자아를보호하기위한수단으로 9 (Inhibition)이라는방어기제를사용한다 . 보다효과적인언어습득을위해서는억압의기제를적절한수준으로낮추어야하는데이를위해교사는수업중 guessing game,communication game& 진행할수 있다.The extent to which individuals build defences to protect their egos.People vary in how adaptive their language egos are, i.e., how able they areto deal with the identity conflict involved in L2 learning. When people beganto speak their native language, they have learner to understand themselvesin their own language. The close connection between language and ego iscalled language ego: the way language helps you to understand and expressyourself,Chapter 04 학습자변인 _ 1271ChapterHow to Low Inhibition* to play guessing games and communication games* to do role-play and skits* to sing songs* to use plenty of group works* to laugh with your studentsᆞ to have students share their fears in small groups(2) Anxiety긴장감에는언어습득을 BASE facilitative anxiety2t 학습을 Aas debilitative87401088 자 있다. 교사는학습을저해하는불안감이나초조감등은 없애고, 경쟁심Ho등을자극하여학습을촉진하는긴장감을활용하도록 한다.He.Learner anxiety is the feeling of worry, nervousness, and stress. Anxiety isnot always a negative factor in learning like many other factors; low levelshelp, whereas high levels hurt.(01) Facilitative (helpful) Anxiety motivates learners to fight the new learningtask, prompting them to make extra efforts to overcome their feelings ofnayanxiety.@) Debilitative (harmful) Anxiety causes the learners to flee the learning taskin order to avoid the source of anxiety.(3) Risk-takingRisk-taking®|]@ © 43= 약것을말하는데적절한수준의위험감수는성공적인 GSHtakingS 위한수업분위기조성을위하여교사는자발적 SSS 장려하고유창성에초점을둔활동을많이활용하도록 한다.122 Build-up 영어교육론 LGuideline for Pre-service TeachersRisking-taking is an important characteristic of successful of secondlanguage. Acculturation Model문화변용 (8004101781404/ 이란제 2 언어학습과함께학습하게되는제 2 언어의문화와제 2 의 AAA (identity) S 통한문화동화를뜻한다 . 문화변용에가장큰영향을끼치는요인으로는사회적거리감 (60081 01868006) 과심리적 712] (psychological. distance)®| ᅵ 있다.Chapter 04 학습자변인127ChapterAcculturation means the process of becoming adapted to a new culture.According to Acculturation Model, second language learning involves theacquisition of a second identity and requires learning the culture of thatcommunity and adapting to those values and behavioral patterns. The extent towhich learners acculturate depends on two sets of factors: social distance andpsychological distance, which limit acculturation, and thus inhibit L2 learning.(1) Social distance : The cognitive and affective proximity of two cultures thatON ie( come into contact within an individual.@) Psychological distance : The extent to which individual learners aregroup dimension.2. 문화변용의단계Ao01) S27} 행복감 : A period of excitement and euphoria over the newness ofthe surroundings.@ 문화충격 (64076 shock) : 자신의문화와목표문화간의차이를인식Individuals feel the intrusion of more and more cultural differences intotheir own images of self and securitys}2f24(culture stress) : 문화충격이점진적으로회복되면서맞는문화적긴장의"에너 노지100]터 = &e E 2 ent =단계. 초기에아노미 (34010416. cultural homeless) 현상을 겪는다.0) 문화동화 (30040 따헤 00) : 문화충격에서완전히회복되어목표문화에동화되고제 2 의자아를갖게 된다.Near or full recovery either, assimilation or adaptation, acceptance of the@new culture and self-confidence in the “new” person that has developedin this culture.3. Students are led in discussion in order toON 아아ae or gam ag ate 8understand how misunderstandings arise when wrong conclusionsare reached about the target culture on the basis of one’s own culturalunderstanding.=e Further readingSapir-Whorf Hypothesis ᄂ ..., C Ag 9 AhougitThe Sapir-Whorf hypothesis suggests that both thought and language |are determined by! culture, For example, culturally determined phenomena“such as the time of events of the color or shape of objects might becomeespecially important for grammar learning in a given language, and, byextension, in thinking as well. Known as linguistic determinism, thisposition refers to the idea that people’s thought processes are culturallydetermined by the features of the language they speak. However,research indicates that the strong version of the Sapir-Whorf hypothesis,that language determines though, is unsupported whereas the weakversion has significant implications for intercultural communication. If aconcept exists in one language but cannot be expressed easily in another,Chapter 04 학습자변인 ^ 29Chapterthis difference may have an impact on cognitive style and the ease ofcross-cultural communication involving the concept. For example, it hasbeen suggested that Chinese or Japanese ESL/EFL learners might avoidusing articles since their languages lack this grammar form. Likewise,teachers must be aware of learners’culturally determine rhetorical patttenpreferences when teaching academic writing in ESL/EFL classes.| ae Further readingAge & Acquisition결정적. 시기가설 ([1(6 Critical Period Hypothesis)O] 따르면인간이언어를학습하는 a 보다용이하게 GSH 수있는시기는생물학적으로혈정뇌어 있으며, 이시기가지나면언어습득이점점어려원진 다.According to the Critical Period Hypothesis, animals including humansare genetically programmed to acquire certain kinds of knowledge andskill at specific times in life. Beyond those critical periods, it is eitherdifficult or impossible to acquire those abilities. With regard to language,the CPH suggests that children who are not given access to languagein infancy and early childhood will never acquire language if thesedeprivations to on for too long.1. 신경학적인 BAA(behaviorism view) — Hemispheric Lateralization사춘기이전의어린아이는뇌의유연성으로인해모국어뿐아니라제 2 언어를 SSS 수있다. 그러나사춘기이후의학습자는뇌편중화가완료되면서좌뇌위주의 loka 하게되므로제 2 언어학습에서원어민과같은발음을쉽게습득하지못하며언어학습을지나치게분석적인과업으로수행 한다.The plasticity of the brain prior to puberty enables children toacquire not only their first language but also a second language andthat possibly it is the very accomplishment of lateralization that makesit difficult for people to be able ever again to easily acquire fluentcontrol of a second language, or at least to acquire it with what iscalled “authentic” (nativelike) pronunciation.130 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers a Pa2. 인지적 SA(cognitive view)인간의인지는생후 164 동안급속도로발달하며성인이된후에는그속도가 줄어든다.As the child matures into adulthood, the left hemisphere (whichcontrols the analytical and intellectual functions) becomes moredominant than the right hemisphere (which controls the emotionalfunctions). Read the following <A> and its teaching implication in <B>. Answer thequestion. [서술형]A_ The effect of age on second language acquisition has been extensivelydocumented, the issue being whether younger learners acquire a secondlanguage more efficiently and effectively than older learners. Researchto date has not conclusively settled the issue of age one way or another,largely because the issue is more complex than it might seem at first.In order to investigate this issue, it is necessary to distinguish betweenthe effect of age on the route of acquisition, the rate, and ultimateattainment. Reviews of the available literature concluded that, while agedoes not alter the route of acquisition, it does have a marked effect onthe rate and ultimate success.As shown above, the research argues that the starting age normallyaffect how rapidly the learners acquire the language. Also, youngerlearners are likely to end up being more proficient than older learners.Generally, however, the same target language items are acquired in thesame order | | | | | at which learners areexposed to the target language for the first time.Based on the passage, complete the summary in <B> using FOUR words.| Your answer |136 Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers09. Learner strategies are the key to learner autonomy, and that one ofthe most important goals of language teaching should be the facilitation ofthat autonomy.1. Core PrinciplesTraining students to use particular learning strategies indeed improvestheir language performance. If so, how can teachers make use of learningstrategies? The principle goal as a teacher, is to equip the students with senseof what successful language learners do to achieve success and to aid themdeveloping their own unique, individual pathway to success.142 Build-up SomS= 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers re) 1rus |Below are comments from second-year middle school students in reference totheir English class taught by a Korean teacher. Read their comments and followthe directions.JiwonIn my English class, 1 do not want to speak because I cannot say everything~correctly. Actually, in English I do not feel as intelligent, friendly, and charming-as--making mistakes or losing face.When I make mistake, 1 get upset and feel that Ihave failed. Clonguoye ego 4) (debilitone 00000 ©)MinaIn my English class I usually like to think quite a lot before trying to saysomething.So, my partner has to wait a while before she has a turn during our conversations.Thus, no one in my class wants to be partners with me. How can I change mylearning style? C vist taking VY 7JisukI like to carefully analyze what I am reading. So, when there is a lot of newHowever, even though I comprehend what each sentence means, I do not get thegeneral meaning of what Iam reading. ( \wtolerone of om} guity 7 )Based on the comments above, identify what learning style or personality eachstudent has and explain what problems it causes in language learning. Finally,design a learner training for each student to help solve their problems. Useapproximately 350 words (85 lines), 25 points.In class a teacher should first identify whether the learning styles (preference)or personalities students have cause some problems in language learning.If necessary, then, she should plan a lesson where students can tackle theirproblems.Chapter 05 Strategy—based Instruction 143Chapter.Strategy—based InstructionFor example, the three students mentioned above have learning problemscaused by their learning styles or personalities. First, in the case of Jiwon, sheshows personal factors which could have negative effects on language success.For example, Jiwon has a very low level of self-confidence about her ability inEnglish, resulting in high inhibition or the building of defenses around her ego.Also, she does not take the risk of making mistakes. These traits she has willmake her seldom speak in class unless the teacher calls on her. Even though sheis pushed to speak in English, her pronunciation is not very clear resulting inmiscommunication. Second, the others, Mina and Jisuk have difficulties in termsof learning styles. In the case of Mina, since she reflects excessively. she thinksof the right word or grammar pattern and wants to get everything right beforeshe attempt to speak or write. Thus, she is unwilling to take risks. On the otherhand, Jisuk has a high left-brain preference, which focuses on the small pieces ofEnglish such as grammar, vocabulary and pronunciation. Thus, he cannot look atthe whole meaning or intentions of the writer.To solve these problems the three students have, a teacher can plan a learnertraining in class which aims to compensate for a certain style or personalityweakness. For Jiwon, a teacher should sequence techniques from easier to moredifficult so that she can establish a sense of accomplishment. Also, an instructorcan design fluency exercise where errors are not corrected at that time. Foranother, Mina, a teacher should plan small group techniques, role playing andworrying about making mistakes.The last student, Jisuk, can be taught to get the2. Good Language Learner Strategies(1) Strategy 1 : They find a learning style that suit them.Good language learners become aware of the type of L2 learning that suitsthem best. Through they conform to the teaching situation to start with, theysoon find ways of adapting or modifying it to suit themselves.144 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 33] |For example, a successful learner who is not a risk-taker and is left-braindominant and somewhat intolerant of ambiguity recognizes her dominanttraits and resolves to force herself to take more risks, to balance herbrain, and to adopt a more tolerant attitude toward language she doesn’tunderstand.(2) Strategy 2 : They involve themselves in language learning processThey do not passively accept what is presented to them, but go out tomeet it. Thy participate more in the classroom, whether visibly or not. Theytake the initiative and devise situations and language learning techniques forthemselves.(3) Strategy 3 : They develop an awareness of language both as system and ascommunicationThey are conscious not only that language is a complex system of rules,but also that it is used for a purpose; they combine grammatical and.many also seek out opportunities to take part in conversations in the secondlanguage.(4) Strategy 4 : They pay constant attention to expanding their language knowl-edge.They are not content with their knowledge of a second language, but arealways tying to improve it. They make guess about things they do not know;they check whether they are right or wrong by comparing their speech withthe new language they hear; they ask native speakers to correct them.(5) Strategy 5 : They take into account the demands that L2 learning imposesThey realize that L2 learning can be very demanding. It is painful to exposethemselves in the L2 classroom by making foolish mistakes. They perseveresin spite of these emotional handicaps.Chapter 05 Strategy—based Instruction 145Chapter05 Strategy—based Instruction3. How to Teach Strategies in the Classroom(1) Teach strategies through interactive techniquesMany strategies are related to, and actually become, the out wardmanifestation of styles. Here are some suggestions for creating anatmosphere in the classroom in which students fell comfortable and areencouraged to develop their own strategies.1. To lower inhibitions: Play guessing games and communicationgames, do role-plays and skits, sing songs, have them share theirfears in small groups.2. To encourage risk-taking: Praise students for making sincereefforts to try out language, use fluency exercises where errors arenot corrected at that time.3. To build students’ self-confidence: tell students explicitly(verballyand nonverbally) that you do indeed believe in them.4. To help them to develop intrinsic motivation: remind themabout the rewards for learning English, play down the finalexamination in favor of helping students to see rewards forthemselves beyond the final exam.5. To promote cooperative learning: direct students to share theirknowledge, play down competition among students._ 6. To encourage them to use right-brain processing: use movies| and tapes in class, have them read passages rapidly, do skimmingeXercises.7. To promote ambiguity tolerance: encourage students to ask youand each other, deal with just a few rules at a time.146 Build-up 영어교육론 IGuideline for Pre~-service Teachers 33) 18. To help them use their intuition: praise students for goodguesses, do not always give explanations of errors, correct onlyselected errors.9. To get students to make their mistakes work for them: letstudents catch and correct each other’s errors, do not always givethem the correct form.10. To get students to set their own goals: explicitly encourage ordirect students to go beyond the classroom goals, have them makelists of what they will accomplish.@) Use compensatory techniques@ 제 2 언어학습시에는장독립 , 장의존및 좌뇌, 우뇌학습유형이모두필요 하나,한쪽으로지나친유형은제언어학습에방해를줄수도 있다. 따라서한쪽으로지나친제 2 언어학습자에게교사는적절한보상적교수기법을취하여보다효과적인제 2 언어학습을진행해야할 것이다.ᆞ과도한장독립 / 좌뇌지배학습 : : integrative language techniques, retelling stories,과도한장독립형및좌뇌학습자는분석적이고세부적인항목에지나치집중 하므로, 보다전체적인맥락안에서의언어학습을할필요가언어의기능지도를적어도 2 가지이상통합적으로사용할수있는학습활동을통해상호보완할수 있다.^과도한장의존 / 우뇌지배학습 : syntactic or semantic clues searches, scanningfor specific information, information-gap techniques, proofreading __.과도한장의존 , 우뇌지배 a 자들은언어학습시과도하게전체적인 Bers고려하다보니세부적인항목에주목을하지못해정확성이떨어지는경우가많으 므로, 교사는학습자들이보다세무적인항목과부분적인요소에주목을3} 4브교수기법이필요하 다.oO LeChapter 05 Strategy—based Instruction 147Chapter__f 05 Strategy—based Instruction© 성공적인언어학습을하기위하여모호함에대한낮은참을성을갖고있는학습자들에게교사는일정 ~ > 만관용적으로될수 ?것이 아니라, 시간을두고그과제에대한나름대로의사고의과정을전개하도록하는 brainstorming,retelling stories, role-play, skimming task 등의기법을통해모호함에대한관용적인태도를길러줄수 있다.[에A.aap=¥NacyrarunN2HIafae|내오x2,Ni(9 중동형학습자에게는 & 더정확한 2A 의해추측을할수있도록길잡이역할을해야할 것이며, 숙고형학습자에게교사는보다시간을두고과제를진행할수있도록인내심을 ste 할 것이다.ᆞ과도한충동형 : making inference, syntactic or semantic clue searches,inductive rule generalization과도한충동성에사로잡힌 sorte 언어학습시너무자신의직관에의존한언어를사용하므로잘못된추측으로인한오류의소지가 많다. 따라서교사는정확한근거에의해추측을추촉을할 수: 제록추론하는방법 SS 지도해야 한다,ᆞ과도한심사숙고형 : small group techniques, role-play, brainstorming,fluency techniques과도한 ee 인학습자들은언어사용시오류를두전하는경우가많으 므로, 교사는학습자들이위험시도 (46-1819709) 를할수있도 aa초점을맞춘교수수기법 (14600 techniques) 위주로의미 SAS) al } 습을하도록 한다. aon(3) Administer a strategy inventoryee ANOLE rarer다양한학습전략을구분하기위한질문목록으Le TM “Ie활용함으로써학생들의학습전략에대한 las 3HuStrategy inventoryS다.A strategy inventory is an extensive questionnaire covering fifty separate이루어여스aT32 oNrotiestrategies in six major categories. By doing so,teachers will increase opportunities for strategic investment in theirlearning process.eius <Learning strategies are divided into what have come to be known as direct orcognitive strategies, which learners apply directly to the language itself, andindirect or metacognitive strategies, in which learners manage or control theirown learning process.(01) Direct strategies include a number of different ways of* remembering more effectively* using all cognitive processes* compensating for missing knowledge@ Indirect strategies include* organizing and evaluating learning* managing emotions« learning with others4. Different Models of SBI@ As part of a standard communicative methodology, teachers help studentsto become aware of their own style preferences and the strategies thatare derived from those styles. Through checklists, tests, and interviews,teachers can become aware of students’ tendencies and then offer adviceon beneficial in-class and extra-class strategies.@) Teachers can embed strategy awareness and practice into their pedagogy.As they utilize such techniques as communicative games, rapid reading,fluency exercises, and error analysis, teachers can help students bothconsciously and subconsciously to practice successful strategies.Chapter 05 Strategy—based Instruction 149Chapterae | 05 Strategy—based Instruction@) Certain compensatory techniques are sometimes practiced to helpstudents overcome certain weaknesses. Therefore teachers need toprovide diagnostic instruments and procedures for determining students’references, and exercises that help students to overcome certain blocks orto develop successful strategies they are weak.@ Teachers can use textbooks that include strategy instruction as part of acontent-centered approach.ous | :Developing Students Self—Awareness of Styles@ Informal self-checklistsOne effective way to instill student awareness of successful styles is throughan informal self-checklist that students fill out and then discuss.(2) Formal personality and cognitive style testsIf formal personality or cognitive style tests are available. teachers might tryusing them but with caution because these tests are often culturally biasedand have difficult language.(8) Readings, lectures, and discussionsAnother way of encouraging self-awareness of styles in the classroom is forteachers to assign occasional readings, or give mini-lectures or presentationsfollowed by discussions about successful learning styles.@ Encouraging “good language learner” behaviorAnother form of instilling s¢ifawareness in students is through frequentimpromptu reminders of “rules” for good language learning and encout-agement of discussion or clarification. Sometimes the little comments fromteachers have the effect of urging students to take charge of their owndestiny by understanding their own styles of learning and capitalizing ontheir abilities. |150 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers iS) aé| ly In the ClassroomLearning Styles ChecklistCheck one box in each item that best describes you. Implications0 교사들은학생들뿐만아니라자신의 teaching 스타일과전략을평가해야 한다.* Teachers could benefit by assessing the learning styles and the strategyuse of their students, because such assessment leads to greaterunderstanding of styles and strategies.* Teachers also need to assess their own styles and strategies, so that theywill be aware of their preferences and of possible biases.ᆞ Self-report Surveys, observations, interviews, learner journals, dialoguejournals, think aloud techniques and other measures can be used.@ 교사가학생들의학습스타일을잘알면학생들에게필요한학습전략을제시할수있다.ᆞ The more that teachers know about their students’ style preferences, themore effectively they can orient their instruction, as well as the strategyinstruction that can be interwoven into language instruction, matched tothose style preferences.* Without adequate knowledge about their individual students’ stylepreferences, teachers cannot systematically provide the neededinstructional variety.@ 어떤한가지교수법이모든학생들에게적합한것은아니라는 AS 명심해야 한다.ᆞ 560166 and strategies help determine a particular learner’s ability andwillingness to work within the framework of various instructionalmethodologies.ᆞ Instead of choosing a specific instructional methodology, teachers woulddo better to employ a broad instructional approach. Such an approachallows for deliberate, creative variety to meet the needs of all studentsin the class.152 Build-up Soims= 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers & =@ 교사들은여러방법으로전략기반수업을준비해야 한다.* Teachers should consider various ways to prepare to conduct strategyinstruction in their classes. Helpful preparatory steps include takingteacher development courses, finding relevant information in print or onthe Internet, and making contacts with specialists.Pe ius | | ^Think Aloud Technique (60080To investigate learner strategies, teachers can let learners think aloud asthinking processes or strategies they are making used of. For example, whilewriting a composition, a student may record his or her thoughts into a taperecorder during the planning, drafting, and revision of the composition. Later,the recording may be used to determine the planning or revision processesused by the student.T : Today, we are going to work on a learning strategy. Learning this strategywill improve our comprehension and the speed at which we read. Well,I’m going to hand out a reading passage. Let us listen in. What I do firstis read the title. I try to figure out what the passage is about. I look atthe subheadings and pictures, too, if there are any. I ask myself what Iknow about the topic and what questions I have. Next, I read the firstparagraph.I don’t read every word, however, I let my eyes skim it veryquickly- just picking out what I think are the main ideas. I especiallylook at the content or meaning — bearing words — usually the nounsand verbs.> 교사가자신의읽기과정을소리내어단계적으로제시하고 있다.Chapter 05 Strategy—based Instruction 153Chapter154Strategy—based InstructionComplete the following table after reading the textWhat did you do during reading?made prediction /formed pictures vused analogy vfound problem ”used fixed-ups J> 학생이사용한 7|ZA(thinking process)S 체크리스트에표시함으로써자신의 MEFS파악할수 있다.A)ly In the Classroom1. 1. Strategy Type 1: Metacognitive - — Plan your time| Level : tnteniiediate or aboveTime : 50 minutesAim _: For students to consider ways in which they can learn, English outside the classroom' Preparation : Make photocopies of the task sheet for your class._ Teaching ProcedureStep 1 : Arouse student interest in the planning task._ Step 2 : Set up the initial pair work and give the students five to tenminutes to discuss, add to, or modify the list of suggestions.Step 3 : When the initial discussion is over, you should facilitate| the setting up of groups. Make OHTs or posters availableto help the groups present their ideas.Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers a 3_ Task sheet_ Here is a list of techniques that people use to help hem learn| English outside the classroom:! * memorizing a list of words| * reading a grammar book- doing grammar exercises| * reading a book or magazine in English0 recopying things from their class notebook* correcting mistakes made in written work* preparing the next unit of the coursebook| Work with a partner and add any others of your own. Strategy type : Metacognitive — Advance organization_ Level : Intermediate_ Time : 50 minutes ,Aim_: For students to improve their reading by learning to preview _ 3: and to Skim to get the Bish of a reading passageChapter 05 Strategy—based Instruction 155Chapter05 Strategy—based Instruction156! Teaching Procedure- Step 1 : Learning journals & Interview. Prior to the lesson the teacher has been reading the students!learning journals, where the students regularly write about whatand how they are learning. The teacher has also been interviewingthe students.. Step 2 : Decision of the strategy of advance organization_ The teacher decides to have students work on the strategy of ;| advance organization. He thinks that they need to improve their 」| 6090108 by preview and to skim to get the gist of a. reading“aloud demonstration..He begins the class with a presentation. He tells students that :they are going to work on a learning strategy called advance |- organization. He begins by modelling. He distributed a reading :| passage.‘What I do first is read the title. I try to figure out what the_ passage is about. I look at the subheadings and pictures, too, if 」: there are any. I ask myself what I know about the topic and what| questions I have. Next, I read the first paragraph. I don't read very ,; word, however. I let my eyes skim it very quickly-just picking out :: what I think are the main ideas. I especially look at the content or! meaning-bearing words-usually the nouns and verbs'. The teacher, calls out the words that he considers key in the first paragraph. 'Fromdoing these things, I know that this passage is about wild horses.| I do not know very much about the topic, but from skimming thefirst paragraph, I have gotten the impression that the passage is| about the challenges of catching and taming wild horses’.Build-up 영어교육론 I. Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) ,Step 4 : The students practice the new learning strategy.‘Td like you to practice just this much now. I am going to handout a new reading passage for you to practice on. When you get ᆞit, keep it face down. Don’t read it yet. Does everyone have one? |Good. Now remember, before you turn the paper over, you aregoing to be practicing the strategy that I have just introduced.| Ready? Turn over the paper. Take a look. Now quickly turn it facedown again. What do you think that this passage is about? Who -can guess? One student says he think that it is about whales. ‘Why |_ do you think so?’ asks the teacher. The student says he has guessedfrom the title, which is ‘Rescuing the World’s Largest Mammal.’What do you think is meant by “rescuing”? the teacher asks, Noone knows so the teacher asks them to keep this question in mindas they read. Turn your page over again. Read through the first -paragraph quickly. Do not read every word. Skip those you don’t |know the meaning of. Do not use your dictionary.’ The teacher |gives the students two minutes to read the first paragraph. He then —asks, ‘Who can tell us what the main idea of the passage is—what |is the gist?” A student replies that the passage is about certain types _of whales being put on the endangered list. ‘That’s a good guess’says the teacher.Step 5 : The students evaluate their own success in learning thestrategy. They modify the strategy to meet their ownlearning needs.Next the students evaluate how they have done. Some feel |distressed because they still feel that they need to understand veryword. However, others are feeling better because they realize that 」their reading assignments need not take as long as they have beentaking. Students may valuea task because they find it intrinsically interesting, because they find itapplicable to their lives or both. Teachers try many ways to gain students’intrinsic: interest in academic tasks, including using authentic literature,choosing activities that might be fun for students, and focusing on contentthat has cultural relevance.(2) Expectancy학생들은과업에서성공할수있다는기대감을가질경우동기부여를더받게 된다:그러므로학생들이성공을경험할수있는기회를제공해야 한다.flOver years of exposure to learning experiences, students develop overallexpectations for success or failure in school. Thus students often have anoverall feeling of being a “good student” or “bad student”. Most high schoolstudents can identify areas that they think they are “good at” and “bad at”.Each day in a classroom can reinforce a student’s expectations influenceeach future encounter in that field. Thus it is critical to ensure that studentsexperiences successes in the classroom. It is important to have tasks that areappropriately challenging-not so difficult that students cannot experiences to“rrappropriate strategies can help students experience success on challengingand - meaningful tasks and can eventually lead to higher expectations oflearning process.(3) Self-EfficacyChapter 05 Strategy—based Instruction 159Chapter0 [ [ 5 | Strategy—based InstructionSelf-efficacy is the specific confidence that one is capable of successfullycompleting a particular task. Self-efficacy is at the core of motivation, self-esteem, and self-regulation. The development of self-efficacy is tied closelywith effective use of learning strategies. Students with high self-efficacy haveconfidence that they can solve a problem because they have developedstrategies for the task that have worked for them in the past. They believethat the more they learn and practice, the more their capabilities willimprove, and they understand that mistakes are just a part of learning. Incontrast, students with low self-efficacy think that they have inherent lowability. They believe that effort will reveal their own inability, and theychoose easy tasks to try to avoid making mistakes. Building students’ strategicawareness can help them see that they are capable of solving problems whenthey use the correct tools. In second language research, correlation havebeen found between students’ reported learning strategies use and their self-efficacy, in particular their beliefs about their own effectiveness as language니이 emus wena 와 00000learners.(4) Attribution전략기반수업은학생들에게그들이적절한전략을사용할경우성공할수있다는것을보여줌으로써학생들의성공혹은실패에대한관여도 (3600164000/ 를바꿀수있Students’ approach to school tasks can depend on the factors to which theyattribute their success or failure. Less often, students may attribute schoolsuccess to effort or, even more appropriately, to effective strategies, Strategiesinstruction helps to alter students’ attributions by showing them that they cansucceed if they use appropriate strategies and, conversely, that their failurecan be attributed to the lack of effective strategies use rather than the lack ofability.Teachers can identify the strategies that best meet their students’ immediateneeds, they can explore students’ reactions to their instructional approaches,and they can use classroom research as a tool for showing students thatstrategies really work.160 Build-up 영어교육론 1#)ly In the Classroom1. Cognitive—inductive ReasoningIn an inductive approach to learning, students are given access todata, and are provided with structured opportunities to work out rules,principles, and so on for themselves. This strategy is essential if learners are to copeeffectively in genuine communicative situations outside the classroom. Itis important for learners to realize that native speakers use this strategyquite naturally when communicating with one another, that it is, in fact,impossible as well as unnecessary to process every single word in mostlistening situations.Listen for NumbersRead these questions about the story asking How far an How long.Then listen to the story again and answer the questions.1.
