The linguistic objective of the lessons is the language of coercion, e.g.the expressions make someone do something, (not) let someone do something, beallowed to do something and the modal structure ‘have to’.@ PPP 0 A focus on one a two forms ove 애마 4o be incorpyotd in the Pertamarce of a Ommunicric원 This 5 on Bim Comes before leaves Cagoge in Co wmupiCotie” ochury, 00809: 70005 0001 of leover longuage is strict in the 0007 stages orl 9100) 7 위 000 :@ “the sucess is judged Th teams of whether er 70% JeotCls Alo produce the to19e4 fog mg with onOtte pfoble jevel s€ . oy. :Lesson Procedure of PPP model 2Integrating grammar using a PPP model Untermediate level)Step 1The teacher uses a generative situation to provide a ¢ontext for thetargeted language. In this case she introduces two characters, Tom andViv, and tells the class that when he was young, Tom’s parents werevery strict. Viv, on the other hand, had very easygoing parents. Forexample, she says, Tom had to help with the housework. But Viv didn’thave to help with the housework. Tom’s parents made him take pianolesson. He didn’t want to, but they made him. Viv, on the other hand,wanted to have a motorbike. Her parents let her have one... Then, theteacher asks the class to report back what they can remember her sayingabout Tom and Viv. She elicits on to the board the following sentences,shaping them into their correct form:@ TRIO Teacher does yoy ottempt ts Conteo| lene lanyvoge© The success is Judged on wherper o> prt [eoynels communitote suc esstoll7,@ At some Hages, leorners ord leocheus wy) focug on language ,“f he lps learners te Shaye and cluty Whe they wont to say.® Foevt on tam Comes alter focus on weonlyg ,Chapter 06 2443-185Chapter1861. He had to help with the housework.2. His parents made him take piano lessons.3. He wasn’t allowed to stay out late.4, Viv didn’t have to help with the housework.5. Her parents let her have a motorbike.6. She was allowed to stay out late.The teacher then elicits paraphrases of each of the six sentences andwrites them on the board. For example:la. His parents made him help with the housework.2a. He had to take piano lessons.3a. They didn’t let him stay out late.The teacher erases the first set of sentences and asks students, in pairs,if they can reconstruct them from memory. Students write the sentencesand these are read out and checked in open class.Step 3The teacher sets a group-work task. The object is to find out who, intheir groups, went to the strictest, and who to the most easygoing,school. Students prepare questions to ask each other using the targetlanguage forms and finally report back to the teacher. A general classdiscussion follows, as to the merits or not of a strict education.The lesson is plotted along PPP lines, with Step 1 being the presentation,Step 2 the (controlled) practice and Step 3 the freer production.niemorable than a straight explanation. The practice stages involve theoe 9494Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers &students first of all transforming and then céconstructing the modelsentences (Step 2). This is done as a written exercise, allowing studentsreflection _time/as well as the chance to work collaboratively. It isprobably at the stage when the students are reading out their sentencesthat the teacher would start to fine-tune for accurate pronunciation.The fluency task (Step 3) is still relatively controlled, but by having thestudents ask and answer a lot of questions using the target languagethere is built-in repetition. Moreover, there is a cCGmmunicative purposeto the task, ensuring a focus on meaning as much as on form.Lesson Procedure of TBIIntegrating grammar using a task-based instruction Untermediate level)Step 1 : pré-taskThe teacher introduces the theme by telling a short anecdote about herschool days, which demonstrates, for example, the relaxed approach tothe dress-code operating in her school. She uses this story to check themeaning of easygoing and its opposite, strict.Step 2: task 05016The teacher invites one or two learners to recount related experiences.She suggest that many people react against a strict upbringing by adoptingvery easygoing attitudes as parents, and vice versa. Since there is someargument about this, she suggests that the class conduct a(survey] in whichthey canvass each other to see if there is any correlation between previous (|experience and present attitudes. She organizes the class into pairs toprepare questions, which they write down. Then, the teacher organizes thepairs of students into groups of four, and asks them to try out their questions (on each other, and to make a mental note of the answers. She monitors theinteractions, noting down examples of student productions that could beimproved, but she doesn’t correct them at this point.ᅵ ...... sos ti|5때Chapter 06q teraction )187ChapterStep 3: past-task01) The teacher asks the class to listen to a recording of some fluentEnglish speakers chatting on the same theme. The conversationincludes various examples of the language of coercion. The teacherasks some general gist questions about the conversation — forexample, which of the speakers had a strict upbringing, which had aneasygoing one? She then hands out a transcript of the recording, andreplays the tape while they read.inner stair Soman te ECSmight be useful in the survey y task, particularly language related to thenotions of being strict and easygoing. They list these in two columns:adjectives and verbs. Students work in pairs on this task, and then theteacher elicits ideas on to the board. For example:Adjectives Verbstolerant I was allowedhe made meI won't let themShe then asks the class to complete the blank spaces after each verb, andto make(generalizations wbout t the grammar of the verbs, She also elicitsthe question forms of the verb structures: were you allowed to. ..? etc.Step 4The students then return to their survey task — but are first given achance to redraft and refine their questions in pairs. They are then pairedSnotoff with different students than the ones they were talking to earlier GnStep 2). The teacher then asks students, working in their original pairs,‘a ase 건question: How does “upbringing affect attitudes? Individual students areasked to present their report to the class. A general discussion ensues.188° Build-up 영어교육론 LGuideline for Pre-service Teachers 3) agThe lesson is a task-based one because, rather than being plottedaround a pre-selected item of grammar, the purpose of the lesson is toachieve a task outcome; in this case, deciding how upbringing affectsattitudes. While this may seem contrived — just as contrived, in fact, aspoate atpre-selecting a grammar item — it could be argued that the task focusencourages learners to take more Geative | (risks with their language.They needn't restrict themselves to the teacher's grammar agenda (as inSample lesson 1): theoretically, they could choose any language fromthe sample text (Step 3). Finally, and most importantly, a task invests the7) pont Wore teorrer- ve 04680 , guecherac, wean ings |lesson with an intrinsic interest, apart from a concern only for language.The language is simply a means, not an end in itself (as is so often thecase in PPP-type lessons).It should be clear that this task-based lesson shares many of theingredients of the PPP lesson, but that the order is radically different: themajor difference being that the production stage is brought to the frontof the lesson (Step 2) after an initial introduction to the theme (Step 1):The lesson starts in the deep end, as it were. The production stage actsas a (rial run, where learners attempt to put into words the meaningsthey wish to express. The problems they have doing this should motivatethem to look for solutions in the sample text (Step 3), That is, they havean incentive to use the text as a resource, and may be better primed fornoticing features 0 of the text than ff they had just read it for the sake ofreading it. The teacher’s role is to guide students (Step 3-@)) to noticefeatures that she herself has diagnosed as being misused or underusedin the trial run. Students are then ready, theoretically, to re-attempt the task(Step 4). As a final push towards accuracy, the report stage Step 4), inwhich the students ‘go public’, imposes an element of formality that forcesattention on to form.=]itkChapter 06189Chapterrp Sued wader (€ needs) : |g os 0 by~ product of 10039 bout1€.3. The blocks are arrangedin rows. Each block is a different color. This is a sound-color chart. Eachrectangle represents one English sound. There is a white horizontal lineapproximately halfway down the chart separating the upper rectangles,which represent vowel sounds, from those below the line, whichrepresent consonant sounds. Without saying anything, the teacher pointsin succession to each of five blocks. Again, no one says anything. Thethird time, the teacher does the pointing, he says /a/ as he touches thefirst block. The teacher continues and taps the four other blocks of colorwith the pointer. FeaturesBE* It includes a particular sequence of commands, all centering on a single topic.Ex.. Topic : Set the table“go to the cupboard, open the cupboard door, find the largest bowl,take it out, set it on the table”ᆞ The teacher demonstrates the appropriate responses to the commands,using whatever realia are available to make the actions comprehensible.ᆞ The students are invited to comply with the commands.*It can include cultural learning in the lessons. Various istoms involving- eating, preparing food, telephone conversations, and introductions aretaught through a series of commands given in the context of real or pretendsituations.02. Benefits* The vocabulary, structures, and syntax of the language used in their lessonswere reinforced by exposure to the audio-motor strategy.* Students became strongly interested in the lessons through the physicalacting out of cultural aspects.ᆞ The lessons, even though designed for the development of listening skills,had a real impact on oral production. The teachers noticed increasedspontaneity and better pronunciation, although they admitted the latter wasdifficult to verify.* The nonnative teachers of the various languages felt that they improvedtheir own skills with the languages they were teaching.Chapter 0625rt199ChapterALAR 4 BD ~~~ -~=-~------- === nnn nee nn nen enn eens,2012 학년도기출 _ ᅵTwo middle school English teachers instruct their classes._ Teacher A : “Today I'll going to show you how to set a table. Zp imerhional Chee on Fav)@ 수업단계@ Comprehension (Pre-production)이단계에서학생들은침묵기 (6160 period)S 가지며교사로부터이해가능한언어입력을받아들 인다.ᆞ During this first stage, the students go through a silent period. Theyreceive comprehensible input usually from the teachers. Often thetotal physical response is used.ᆞ Simple responses to the comprehensible input may be made bygesturing, nodding, using the L1, answering “yes,” or “no,” givingnames of people or objects as answers to questions.- A lot of visuals, explanations, and repetitions are used.* The teacher’s speech is a little slower than usual. The intonationis reasonably normal except that key words receive a bit of extraemphasis.* Students are not called upon to respond individually. Instead,questions are directed to the whole group, and one or several canrespond.. Kéy terns are written on the board, perhaps on the second or thirdtime the students are exposed to them.Chapter 06 7441-201Chapter(6) Early speech production두번째단계에서학생들은점점발화를시작하면서자신들의중간언어를발달시키고정교화 한다. a)*The second stage generally begins with an extension of manyactivities used in the comprehension stage such as the sentence-completion response, in which a personalized question is asked andthe answer is provided except for one word.« Students gradually answer “Mike has dress” instead of just “Mike” toteacher’s question “Who has on a blue dress?”* The speech at first will contain many errors which should be dealtwith only. ‘indirectly, for example, “Yes, Mike has on the dress”,instead of “No, you should say, Mike has on the dress.”© Speech emergence학생들의발화에이미변화가시작되었기때문에두번째단계와세번째단계를나누는것이다소모호하지만이단계에서는학생들의오류가점점줄어들점점어렵고 SAA 과제를통해서발화를계속확장해 나간다.ᆞ The utterances become longer and more complex. Many errors are stillmade but, if enough comprehensible input has been internalized, theyshould gradually decrease as the students move toward full production.* A large number of activities can be used that are somewhat moredemanding and challenging but still within reach cognitively: music,poetry, role-playing, drama, affective activities, and problem-solving.ᆞ Many of the activities can be extended to provide additional opportunitiesfor development. For example, instead of simply answering questionsabout an application form/ the students can now fill one out; instead ofjust following directions, they can begin to write their own sets of simpledirections/to see if others can follow them.202 Build-up 영어교육론 |Guideline for Pre-service Teachers esLesson Theme: Body parts and ailmentsStudent level: beginner levelTeaching ProcedureStep 1: Teacher displays visual of a person with body part labeled.She begins by pointing to words and saying body parts (studentsrepeat words only if comfortable with language).Step 2: Teacher removes labels, distributes them, and has each learneraffix label to correct body part.Step 3: Teacher removes cards again. Students in class have a set of yes/ _no cards (yes one color, no anther color). Teacher points to and says a body :part, sometimes correctly and sometimes incorrectly. Learners hold up yes/no card according to whether the teacher said the right or wrong word.Lesson Theme: Washing A CarTask type: problem solvingStudent level: intermediate levelTeaching ProcedureStep 1: The teacher will guide the students in developing the vocabulary :oybyianecessary to talk about the activity. -rag, water, park, bucket, sponge,drivewayStep 2: Then together the class and instructor create utterances to describe :the sequence of events to complete the activity. The class might say: !— First I look for a bucket and a sponge or some rags.— Then I park the car in the driveway.— 7 use the hose to wash the car first with water only.Chapter 06 교수법 ^ 703ChapterThese utterance are developed slowly with interspersed discussion.— Which is better to use, a sponge or a clean rag? :— Should you use soap or other cleaners (such as detergents) to wash a car? 01Step 3: After sequence is constructed, the discussion will broaden toinclude questions and discussion concerning the specific activity inthe students’ own lives.— How often do you wash your car? when? / where? / Do you enjoy it? /Why? / Why not?@® 시사점(@ What Teachers Do :* Conduct class primarily in the target language.* Use gestures, pictures, props, and dramatic flair.ᆞ Engage students in conversation. > prducd~« Maintain a lively atmosphere.« Supply interesting and comprehensible input such as stories and jokes.* Use small-group and role-play activities.* Encourage students to answer in any way they can or want to.- Explain grammar as students have questions. DefinitionAuthentic materials: 목표문화권의화자에의해생성된담화및글을의미하는것으로, 현재진행되는외국어교실수업에서의학습자료로선택해야할것인지에3대한찬반이엇갈리고 있다. 따라서교사는학습 24a authentic materialS 선택할경우장단점을명확하게파악하고학습자의순준을고려 하여, 어떻게 authenticmaterial& 교실수업에서제시해야할것인지를생각해야 한다.There are number of definitions related to authentic materials; (07 anauthentic text is a stretch of oral language, produced by a real speakeror writer for a real audience and designed to convey a real message ofsome sort @) authentic texts (either written or spoken) are those whichare designed for native speakers; they are text designed not for languagestudents, but for the speakers of the language in question, and @ a rule ofthumb for authentic specially produced for propose of language teaching.226 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers 2 3)oly In the ClassroomRole PlaySITUATION 1: AN EVENING’S VIEWINGWork in pairs or groups of three.You want to watch television tonight.Look through the following Programme Guide and try to decide which pro-gramme to watch.One person starts: ‘What shall we watch tonight?’Programme guideby Celia BrayfieldTV/RADIOBBC 1A$2,.3600On the Move. 12.4 ide:1.6,--Pedble ere 146 Pars 내 were.You and 206. 2, 나 Schools, Goheges és 이Hine Witch. Criteria for Selecting Authentic Materials진정성있는자료를선택하는데있어서그자료의눈제가가르치는학생들의요구와Authentic materials are taken from real life and are going to be introducedin the artificiality of the classroom. So a teacher has to ensure that the topicof the authentic materials chosen addresses the needs and interest of theNIE Mie eespecific group of students being taught.. BICS(2) Purpose of language learning < CALP < Comte Acodenve 00868 Pudiacney )자료를선택하는데있어서학생들이영어학습을하는 GAo] 고려되어야 한다,The goal of language learning for that particular group of learners shouldbe kept in mind while deciding which materials to use in class. The teacher can dothis by either extending or expanding.@ Extending : 같은 a 습 내용, 같은수준의연습활동 SS 추가함으로써양적으로만ABS 추가하는방법 이다. (44)The teacher supplies more of the same type of material, thus makinga quantitative change in the material. This means that the techniquesare being applied within the methodological framework of the originalmaterials.? Example 1There is a practice which asks the learner to complete a sentence with themissing verb in the correct form, such as the simple past. The coursebookmay have provided ten sentences for this treatment, but the teacher mayvalue this type of activity for her class and adapt the coursebook byadding five more sentences with missing verbs.0 Example 2The materials contain a practice in the pronunciation of minimal pairs(rice/lice, rake/lake) but not enough examples of the difficulties forlearners with a particular L1. Thus, the teacher put more examples with r-lminimal pairs.@ Expanding : 기존의자료와는다른기능을다룬 AGRE, 다른차원의언어접근법을적용한연습활동을추가함으로써텍스트를질적으로추가하는것을Expanding adds something different to the materials; the change isqualitative. The expanding goes further than extending by putting in adifferent language skill or a new component.234 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers? Example 1The only pronunciation practice in the materials is on individual soundsand minimal pairs, however, this may be necessary but not sufficient.Therefore, the teacher decides to add some work on sentence stress. ( or} AVE)© new! ComperieAlthough the new grammar material is important and relevant, the additionof a discussion section at the end of the unit will help to reinforce andcontextualize the linguistic items covered. (1+ % 세 A423 )L offer lg Stall(2) Deleting기존텍스트에서불필요한부분을생략하는방법 이다. Adding 마찬가지로양적인방법과질적인방법이 있다.Deletion is the opposite process to that of addition by omitting materialsfrom the original.® Subtracting : 동일한언어기능내에서지나치게많은연습활동을생양적으로텍스트를줄이는것을의미 한다.Subtracting refers to reducing the length of materials in quantitative&가하드[0way. It does not have a significant impact on the overall methodology.<? Example 1A teacher decides to do five of the questions practising the simple pasttense instead of the ten in the coursebook.<? Example 2Although a communicative coursebook has been selected as relevant inour situation, some of the language functions are unlikely to be requiredby learners. Such functions as “giving directions” or “greeting” may beuseful; “expressing sympathy” or “ordering things” may not. Thus theteacher decided to skip the activities for latter functions.Chapter 07 교재개발및교재분석 _ 235Chapter@) Abridging : 여러기능을다룬 ASHE 중질적으로 다른, 빨필요한활동을생략하는것을 말한다.Abridging means omitting materials qualitatively, fnaking the changesgreater than subtracting.? Example 1 |The material contains a discussion section at the end of each unit.However, our learners are not really proficient enough to tackle thisadequately. Thus, the teacher may delete this kind of training.0 Example 2Students on a short course are working with communicative materialsbecause of their instrumental reasons such as international business trip orvisit as tourists. The lengthy grammatical explanations accompanying eachfunctional unit are therefore felt to be inappropriate.(3) Modifying학습자의요구나언어접근법에보다적절하게텍스트의내용이나수업의형식적인면을수정하는것을 말한다. ᆞModifying refers to a change in the nature or focus of an exercise, or text,or classroom activity. Currently the most frequently stated requirement for achange is for materials to be made more communicative. Therefore, modifyingmay relate activities more closely to leaners’own backgrounds and interests,introducing models of authentic language.@ Rewriting: 학습자의요구나특정교수법 (특히 CLT) 맞게텍스트의 Wes수정하는기법을 말한다.Rewriting means an internal change that can be applied to any aspect ofcontent.? Example 1Some of end-of-text comprehension questions are more like a test, wherestudents can answer by “lifting” the information straight from the text.These questions can be modified so that students have to interpret whatthey have read or heard.236 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers Ss ”<? Example 2 ᆞA story about an English family, with English names, living in an Englishtown, eating English food and enjoying English hobbies can in fact bemodified quite easily by making a number of straightforward surfacechanges.® Restructuring : 학습상황에보다적합하게학생들의활동이나교실 (혹은 그룹배치를조정하는방법을 말한다.fo) aRestructuring can be applied to classroom management.? Example 1The materials may contain role-play activities for groups of a certain size.It will probable be necessary to assign one role to a number of pupils atthe same time. Obviously the converse—where the class is too small forthe total number of roles available—is also possible.oO Example 2A written language explanation designed to be read and studied can bemade more meaningful if it is turned into an interactive exercise where allstudents participate.(4) Simplifying학습자들의이해를높이기위해서 단어, 문법, 문장길이등옆어의쉬준을조절하는방법을 말한다. :When simplifying, the teacher could be rewording instructions or text inorder to make them more accessible to learners, or simplifying a completeactivity to make it more manageable for learners and teachers. There is adistinct danger of distorting language/vhen attempting to simplify a text andthus making the text inauthentic.(1) Sefitence structure : Sentence length is reduced fr a complex sentence isrewritten as a number of f simpler ones, or example by the replacement ofrelative pronouns by fhouns And ptonouns followed by a main verb.Chapter 07 교재개발및교재분석 37Chapter(8) Grammatical structure : For 0 passives are converted to actives; simplepast tense to simple present; reported into direct speech.(5) Reordering연습활동이나자료의제시순서를교육적인관점에서보다더적합한순서로변경하는방법을 말한다.The teacher make materials more pedagogic sense by sequencing activitiesin a different order.|? Example |Materials typically present “the future” by “will” and “going to”. However, formany students, it is helpful to show the relationship between time referenceand grammatical tense in a more accurate way. The teacher would includethe simple present and the present continuous as part of the notion of“futurity”, using “Next term begins on 9 September” as illustrations.Example 2 |개The teacher can begin with a general discussion before looking at a readingpassage rather than using the reading as 3 basis for discussion.use gPrecautions on Text Adaptation1. 교과서에서 dialogue 다루기전에교실에서유사한 dialogues 구성한 다.This allows for learner input and assures that the language used in the dialogueis within the learners’ reach. Learner-generated dialogues have a strongerconnection to the learners’ lives as they use their own names and places intheir community. The students can compare their dialogue to the one in thetext, providing them with more than one way to express themselves. andcommunicate with others.238 © Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers2. 수업시작전학생들의삶 , 흥미와관련이있는지평가 한다.Evaluate a chapter ahead of time in terms of relevance to learners’ lives and-interest, and prepare visuals and realia that will make the material moremeaningful to your students.. 수업시작 전, 난이도에대해미리평가 한다.Could the vocabulary, grammar, or functional language be more challenging? Ifso, brainstorm other words, forms, or phrases around the same theme that youwant to present and practice. Are there many words that you anticipate willbe particularly difficult in this lesson? If so, be prepared to demonstrate thosewords through multiple means, both visual and aural/oral.cient eee 9. 텍스트에따라적합한학습양식이다를수 있다.Some texts may favor a particular learning style.Think of ways to enhance thelesson to appeal to many learning style preferences. In a lesson on foods,I bringin spices that learners smell, and foods that they can taste. For learners whohave difficulty understanding written or verbal explanations of verb tenses, usesimple time lines to illustrate the meaning of the grammar. Tactile learners maylearn best by using manipulative-realia, flashcards, or picture.. 다중 X|S(multiple intelligences) 고려한 다.A common activity in ESL books is to place information in a sequence, eithera dialogue, or information from a listening or reading passage. Complete the summary by filling in each blank with TWO to SIX wordsfrom the passage. Change the word forms if necessary. [7/22]Conventional wisdom in language teaching suggests that there is nosuch thing as a perfect textbook. This is likely to be true whether thematerials in question were commercially produced or locally createdwithin a given program. Moreover, the task of completely reinventingthe materials for all the courses in a program on a continuous basis is a |_ staggering undertaking. One viable solution to both these problems is: to use what is of value in an existing set of materials, while adapting it- to the needs or changing needs of the program.The first stage in adapting the textbook is to find out whether it servesthe students’ needs and helps meet the course objectives. In so doing,it is important to identify the gaps that cannot be filled by the textbook.Filling the gaps is adapting the textbook. What should the gaps be filledwith? Certainly, teachers in the program may know from their ownexperience existing materials that may help to fill the gaps. Or materialscreation may be necessary for some of the missing elements.Materials adaptation is regarded as a teacher’s attempt to (1)in the textbook by means of commercially available materials or materialscreation. It is usually done because it is extremely difficult to find a perfecttextbook or to (2) regularly.Your answer gm(2)Chapter 07 교재개발및교재분석 5Chapter02. What is one potential problem of using authentic materials mentioned inthe passage? Use Seven to Ten words. [7/2/33]Using authentic materials is one of the mainstays of an imaginativeand motivating higher level course, but rarely features at levels lowerthan intermediate. There are several reasons for this. One is a kindof fear that students will panic when faced with language that islargely unfamiliar, There is a feeling that, to prevent students from' panicking, the language should be edited to the students’ level. This isan unnecessary fear, as using authentic materials can be rewarding andstimulating for both teachers and students.Authentic materials are linguistically difficult, but that’s not thepoint. It is true that authentic materials, written or recorded, are likelyto be too hard even for advanced students. The trick, regardless of thematerials used, is not to edit and grade the materials, but to develop! and use a variety of tasks that suit your students’ abilities. Especially- with lower levels, it needs to be emphasized that students don’t have_ to understand everything in order to perform the set tasks. Students| often don’t believe you until you go through a few tasks with them. Byhelping students “conquer” authentic materials with a variety of tasks,you come to build their confidence in coping with the unknown, animportant element in their development as independent learners.| Your answer |252 ~~ Build-up 영어교육론Guideline for Pre-service Teachers03. Complete the summary by filling in the blank with. [7/22]ESL/EFL teachers have access to a great number of authentic materialsand media. Using authentic materials and media has disadvantagesand advantages. One disadvantage is that it takes time and effort tolocate authentic materials. A second disadvantage is that it is sometimesdifficult to make authentic materials and media comprehensible to thestudents. A third disadvantage is that some students will not acceptauthentic materials and media as being a valuable learning source.Although using authentic materials has disadvantages, there are verystrong reasons to use them. They can reinforce for students a directrelation between the language classroom and the outside world. Inaddition, authentic materials and media offer a way to contextualizelanguage learning.Although authentic materials have disadvantages; they need (1)| 1814(2)[ , is hard to make them (3) | , they have strong advantages;they give student (4)) | and(5)[_ what students learn.[Your answer Igy(2)(3)(4)(5)Chapter 07 교재개발및교재분석 =D 53ChapterO04. Class Size — Large Classes대부분의교사들은언어학습의가장큰걸림돌중의하나가대집단 (18786 classes)수업이라고지적한다 . 그러나현장에있는교사들은이와같은대집단 수업, 즉 , 학생수에변화를주기어려운학습상황에직면하고있으므로주어진학습상황인대집단수업안에서의효율성과변화를고려해볼수밖에 없다.(1) Use pairwork and groupwork학생들의참여를극대화하도록대집단수업을짝활동과소집단활동으로구성하도록한다.When using pairwork and groupwork with large groups, it is important tomake instructions expecially clear, to agree how to stop the activity and togive good feedback.(2) Maximize individual work학생개인의속도와능력에맞춰맞춤과제를제공하도록 한다.Perhaps we can get students to use graded readers as part of theirindividual reading programme. When we get students to build their ownportfolio of work, we are asking them to work as individuals, too. We canencourage students to make full use of a school library or self-access centre.We can get students to write individually — offering their own responses towhat they read and hear. We can direct them to language learning websites,or we can get them to produce their own blogs.260 © Build-up 영어교육론 LGuideline for Pre-servicé Teachers(3) Use students수업중에학생들마다다른책임감을심어주도록 한다.For example, we can appoint class monitors whose job it is to collecthomework or hand out worksheets. Students can take the register or organizetheir classmates into groups. We can ask some of our students to teach theothers. This might mean asking individuals to be in charge of a group whoare preparing arguments for a debate for example, or who are going througha worksheet. It might mean telling individual students that it is their job toexplain some language to their group. We need to choose our student ‘leaders’with care, and we will then monitor their performance very carefully. Thiswill not only be useful for us, but may give them some satisfaction, too, andthis may affect their motivation very positively.(4) Use a different pace for different activities소집단수업에비하여대집단수업에서는 어렵지만, 가급적과업마다속도를조절하도록한[:*If we ask students to say something in a large class, for example, we needto give them time to respond before charging ahead. If we care conducingdrills, we may be able to work at quite a fast pace, but if we are askingstudent to think about something, we will want to slow the pace right down.(5 Menasing Mixed Level Class대집단수업의가장 2 문제점중의하나가학생들의언어능력에차이가난다는것이다. 따라서 sre 능력을지닌학생들 (01160 ability students)S 지도한다는AS 교사에게수업에대한계획및수행상의여러가지문제점을 일으킨다.Many teachers see mixed level classes as especially problematic. Yet in areal sense all classes have students with a mixture of different abilities andlanguage levels. Within the school environments, students are often streamed— that is re-grouped for language lessons according to their abilities. In othersituations, however, such placement and streaming is not possible and soteachers are faced with individuals who have different language knowledge,Chapter 08 Mixed Level Class 261ChapterO'81 Mixed Level Classdifferent intelligences, different learning speeds, and different learningstyles and preferences. There is particular concern for the needs not only ofstudents who are having difficulty at the lower end of the scale, but also for“gifted” students.(1) Communicative teaching principles의사소통적언어교수원리를 Eql= mixed level classS 지도하기위한두가지전제는다음과 같다.@ If students complete the task we set — answering a certain number ofquestions, marking a given number of sentences true or false — we feelthat they have read or listened successfully.@) With a long, complex text, a simple task makes the reading or listeningachievable for weaker students. With a shorter, simpler text, the task canbe more demanding.Text level of challenge + Task level of support = Student success(2) Working with different content상이한언어능력과요구를갖는학생들을지도하는방법중의하나가각학생들에게상이한자료를제공하는 것이다. 즉 , 학생들의수준및요구 ( ᄆ 6608) 에맞춰제공되는자료는학습자개개인의동기와흥미를유발하게될 것이다.© Differentneeds (OQ <9 ® 시트 0009 rge )to 때For example, we might give student A a text form English languagenewspaper about a certain topic. Student B might be directed to a website onthe same topic but wher¢ ane information is not so dense. Student C mightlook at a simplified reader « on the topic, and we might provided student Dwith a short text that we ourselves gave written on the subject, written insuch as way as to be comprehensible to them. In this way, all the student areworking at their own individual levels.262 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachers gg '© Different levelsOne way of offering different content is to allow students to makechoices about what material they are going to work with. For example,we can offer them a range of possible grammar or vocabulary exercisesand they can choose which ones they want to do. If we wish them to readoutside the class, we will encourage them to choose which books theywant to read, since when they make their choice — rather than havingbooks chose for them — they are likely to read with enthusiasm.(3) Drawbacks in a large classGiving students different content is an ideal way to differentiate betweenthem. Nevertheless, it is extremely problematic in large classes. Not onlydoes it involve considerably more teacher preparation time than non-differentiated content have to search out a range of different exercise andmaterials for different individuals, but giving feedback to students in classbecomes a lot more complicated when we are responding to a number ofdifferent tasks than it is when we are giving feedback about one.(3) Different student actions학생들에게상이한자료및내용을제공하기가어려울 경우, 동일한자료에대한한반응및답변을유도하는것도하나의방법이될 것이다. |@® Give students different tasks : 동일한읽기자료를제공하고학생들에게저마다다른답변을하도록요구 한다.For example, group A might have to interpret the information in thetext by reproducing it in graphic form (or in charts and tables). Group B,on the other hand, might answer a series of open-ended questions. Group C— the group we perceive as having the greatest need of support — mightbe offered a series of multiple-choice questions; their task is to pick thecorrect response from two or more alternatives because we think this willbe easier for them than having to interpret all the information themselves.Chapter 08 Mixed Level Class 263Chapter0°34 Mixed Level Class@ Give students different retes : 과제진행시학생들에게저마다다른역할을제시한 다.If students are doing a role-play, for example, in which a police officeris questioning a witness, we might give the student playing the policeofficer the questions they should ask, whereas the student playing thewitness has to come up with their own way of expressing what they wantto say. We will have done this because the students or students playingthe police officer clearly need more guidance than the others. If studentsare preparing for a debate, we might give Group A a list of suggestedarguments to prepare from whereas Group B (whom we think need lesssupport) are told to come up with their own arguments.@® Reward early finishers : 동일한내용의동일한과제를일찍마친그룹에게는관련된추가과제를제공하여흥미와동기유발을유지하도록 한다.@) Encourage different student response : 동일한자료와과제를제공하되 , 학생들의능력에따른결과물 (64[00006/ 을유도할수 있다.We can pick up flexible tasks which make virtue out of differencesbetween students.For example, we ask students to write some true statements containingthe words in, tomorrow, my, hope, the moon and five. Each sentencemust contain one of these words, and the maximum number of sentencesis 12. If, on the other hand, wespend all our time with students who we think need our help more thanothers, the higher-level students may feel neglected and unchallenged.Such students quickly lose interest in the class and develop an attitudewhich makes them difficult to work with.@ Mixed level class 교사들은모든학생들이수업에참여할수있도록유도해야 한다.When setting a task with the whole group (perhaps by asking initialquestions to build up a situation), teachers will want to start by working ata level that all of the students are comfortable with. She will ask questionsthat all the students can understand and relate to so that their interest isaroused and so that they all the students can understand the goal they areaiming for. Once they are all involved with the topic or the task, she mayallow for differentiation in any of the ways. But her initial task is include_and engage everyone — because students who feel they are excluded willsoon start to behave as if they are excluded!@ Flexible groupings : 과제의성격과유형에따라다양하게학생들을소집단활동을유도할수 있다.Sometimes we might put them different groups so that each group can:ttdo different tasks. Eloise doesn’t.4, ? James does.5 ? Chris does.270. Build-up 영어교육론 LGuideline for Pre-service TeachersWith task A, weaker students answer questions about the text. With TaskB, stronger students write questions for given answers related to the text.Because the answers to these two tasks are complementary, it would notbe an efficient use of class time for the teacher to conduct postactivityfeedback with the whole class. Instead, student-students feedback would bea good idea, with the students in AB pairs. The teacher should naturally beavailable as an arbiter if there are any questions of their own. If there aregrammatically correct, and fit the given answers, the teacher should confirmthem as also correct. This type of feedback, in weak/strong pairs, is verymotivating for the weaker students. They have got the difficult questions thatthe strong students have struggled to reconstruct. For weak students, already |knowing key information is a pleasant change from_traditional whole-class—oral feedback, which often turns into a dialogue between the teacher and thebrightest and most forthcoming students._? Each student in a pair has a slightly different version of the same mapof a city, with buildings labelled.2. Two students, higher and lower proficient levels, are grouped in apair, where the former and the latter take the role of the receiver andsender roles respectively.3. The teacher tells students in each pair that the two maps are similar,but that one is older than the other, so you will find that some partsof your maps are different.4. The lower proficient student in each pari is required to tell theirpartner, the higher proficient, a route. The task is completed whenthe student who know the route successfully communicates it to thestudents who doesn’t know it.DescriptionThe activity is designed to generate collaborative language work. Success insecond language learning is related to the learner’s degree of acculturationinto the second language culture. Acculturation hypothesis was one of the firsttheories of SLA that attempted to prioritize social factors over purely cognitiveones.문화변용이란개인이Accuracy 222The extent to which a learner’s use of a second language conforms to the rulesof the language. It is usually measured in terms of grammatical accuracy butit is also possible to talk about accuracy of vocabulary and pronunciation aswell. Accuracy is often contrasted with fluency, which means the capacity tobe communicative in realtime conditions. Accuracy was once thought to be aprecondition for fluency. But to withhold fluency activities until the learners areaccurate is now considered unrealistic. Research into the order of acquisition ofgrammatical structures suggests that accuracy may be “late-acquired”.정확성이란제 2 언어의 문법, 어CLT 이전관점에서는정확성을287 © Build-up 영어교육론 1Glossary튼정 o=o화속으로통합되어가는과정을stress -+ recovery’2| 4 단계를거치게 된다. 문화변용가설은Sapir-Whorf hypothesisOl|A| 출발하 였으며, 문화그에뜻하며,음등의규칙체계와학습자가사용한언어의(fluency)#} 대립되는개념 으로, 유창성을위정확하게언어를사용할때까지유창성을보류 하였다. 그러나현재 CLT 관점에서는보완적인관계로 HT accuracy} fluency 사이의균형을강조한 다.7|# — culture shock — culture언어, 사고, 문화사이에| 정도는제 2 언어Guideline for Pre-service Teachers $3) 「Age and Second language learning 나이와제 2 언어학습과의관계The precise relationship between age and second language learning remainsunresolved and controversial. There are cognitive and maturity differencesbetween children and adults that make a difference in language learning. Therate of acquisition and ultimate level of success varies. However, with regardto grammar, research suggests that the acquisition process is largely unaffectedby age. Its mostdistinctive feature was the drilling of sentence patterns. As in the direct method,spoken language was prioritized; translation and the use of meta-language werediscouraged; and accuracy was considered to be a precondition for fluency.Appendix 01 Glossary 283의학습이론의영향으로대두된구두청각교수법은 SAS 습관의형성이라보고이에따라올바른oO어를습관화하기위한 practice, repetition, memorization, pattern—practice drills7} 수업활동의주를이루고있다. 1950^~~1960 년대 FS 이룬구두청각교수법은 1960 년대 CHEE! 인지주의에의해비판을받았지만현재|JIA교실학습의 minimal pairS 이용한발음 지도, 문법지도에여전히영향을끼치고 있다.Authenticity 진정성A classroom text is authentic if it was written for a non-classroom audience suchas a newspaper article or a pop song, whereas a course book drill or dialogue arenot. According to behaviorism, habits are formed when thelearner’s responses to external stimuli are positively reinforced. To behavioristpsychologists, language was just another kind of behavior, and it could beconditioned. The language teaching method that is associated with behaviorism iscalled audiolingualism. In this method, the stimulus—response-reinforce cycle wasrealized through pattern practice drills. Use of the learners’ L1 was discouraged,since it might lead to bad habits. Errors were avoided for the same reason.Hl22건=ri모Bilingualism 이중언어사용Bilingualism is the use of two languages. Bilingual users of English speak Englishas their second language alongside one or more other languages. Accordingto behaviorist learning theory, the first language interfered with the second.Accordingly, the two languages were kept separate. However, a distinction ismade between additive bilingualism, in which the second language is added tothe first without threatening the speaker’s first language identity, and subtractivebilingualism, in which the second language replaces the first, thereby threateningthe speaker’s first language identity.이중언어사용 (2 개언어 ASS 2 가지의다른언어를사용하는 AS 의미 하지만, 2 개의언어를똑같이우수하게사용하는 AGS 의미하지 않는다. 이중언어 ASS additive bilingualism} subtractive bilingualisme = LhACH.전자는모국어에대한언어정체성에혼란없이목표어를사용하는 AS 의미 하며, 후자는제 2 언어가모국어와모국어에대한정체성을대체하는경우를 가리킨다.Classroom interaction 끄심에서의상호작용Classroom interaction is the general term for what goes on between the peoplein the classroom, particularly when it involves language. In traditional classrooms,Appendix 01 Glossary 285Appendix01most interaction is initiated by the teacher, and learners either respondindividually, or in unison. This is at variance with theview that language is “hard-wired” in the brain, and that the capacity to learnlanguages is something we are born with. A later version of cognitive learningtheory suggests that the child acquires language by forming and testing‘hypotheses about the adult language it hears around it.| 주의학습이론에따르면인간은일종의언어 BS AAS 타고 나며, 4H inputdll 의해자신만의언어( 가설 ) 을형성해나가며언어를습득한다고 보았다. 인지주의학습이론은행동주의학습이론이경시했던그형성를자내부의 mental processOl] 초점을두며 rule—based learning>1 Oy4} ro띠 > 」게IJoCoherence 응집력If a text is coherent, it makes sense. Cohesion is the use ofgrammatical and lexical means to achieve connected text, either spoken orwritten. Unlike coherence, which different readers or listeners may experience tovarying degrees, cohesion is a stable property of text. And while cohesion mayhelp make a text coherent, it cannot guarantee it.결합력이란글의요소들이연관되어있는정도로주로단어의 반복, 상위 단어, 인칭 대명사, 지시대명사의사용등에의해결정된 다. 결합력은응집력을보완하는요소이지만결합력이있다고해서반드시응집력있는 164 라고할수는없다Collocation 연어If two words collocate, they frequently occur together. Most communication strategies are directedat filling in the gaps in the learner’s vocabulary knowledge. If they help thespeakers achieve their intended message, they are labeled achievement strategies.But the speaker might decide that the message is simply not achievable. The shift was away from teaching language systems such as vocabularyand grammar in isolation to teaching people how these systems are used inreal communication; and from viewing linguistic competence alone as beingthe goal of language learning to replacing it with the notion of communicativecompetence. This entailed a major re-think of syllabus design, materials,classroom practice and testing. Thus, communicative terms supplemented, orreplaced, the traditional grammar syllabus with the functional-notional syllabus.b>rah」언|ian =x언어사용의 SIS 기능, - 의사소통에보다 ABS 두고학습자들의상호작용을중시하여등장접근법은언어학습에 SUS 기존의언어의개별적인문법적요소에서의사소통능력으로의관점의가져왔 다. 또한문법요소들로구성된 structure-based 8119046 에서 notional—functional syllabus= 변화했CLT9| strong '6「90/ 은언어를직접사용함으로써언어를학습한다는관점아래 taskbased instruction9| 발전을가져 왔다.rea8화를moCommunicative competence 243 능력Communicative competence is what you know in order to be able tocommunicate effectively. The term contrasts with competence (now known aslinguistic competence), which is the knowledge that enables the creation of well-formed sentences. The conception of competence suggested the need to re-define the goals of language teaching, and to design a methodology to match.Thus, the notion of communicative competence fuelled the development of thecommunicative approach.타인과효과적으로의사소통을하는 SHE 언어의형태에대한지식을기순으로 SE linguistic competence®t반대되는개념으로언어를직접사용하고적절한대화를나눌수있는 SSS 뜻한다 . 전통적인교수에서는linguistic competences 보다중시했지만의사소통적접근법의등장으로언어학습의 SMS 의사소통능력의배양으로하고 있다.288 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service TeachersCommunity Language Learning (CLL) 공동체언어교수법Also called counseling learning, CLL is a teaching method that falls within thehumanistic tradition. In theory, the purpose of comprehension questions is to check learners’understanding of a text. An alternative, more helpful approach, is to set questionsin advance of listening or reading, and which learners answer while reading orlistening. There are two types of conjunction: co-ordinating and subordinating. Co-ordination conjunction, such as “and” and “but”join equivalent units. Subordinating conjunctions such as “if”, “because” and“when” join a subordinate clause to a main clause.접속사는단어와 단어, 구와구 , 문장과문장등을연결하는기능을하는 ASS 말한다. andet but 등의등위접속사와 because, when, if Si} 같은종속접속사가 있다. 접속사는 16 의 cohesionS 강화시키는기능을담당한다Connectionism 연결주의Connectionism is a way of using computers to model the way that the brainprocesses and learns information, including language. Connectionist models arebased upon the way that the brain’s neural networks function by being massivelyinterconnected. Overtime, the connections in the network are strengthenedor weakened according to how frequently they are used, and according towhether the output from the system is correct or not. In this way, connectionsare established and the network “learns”: strong, weak, zero and negativeassociations are built up in the form of connection strengths.연결주의는뇌의정보처리과정으로언어학습을설명하고자 한다. 즉뇌의세포들이새로운정보에대해서로연결된 YS 형성하여정보를받아들이는것처럼언어학습도노출된 어휘, SSS 간의 AAS 형성하여언어를학습하게된다는 것이다. AB 빈도수가높은문구나 SSE 강한네트워크를 Solo 뇌에저장이되고연결횟수가적거나없는표현에는약한네트워크가형성되거나네트워크가형성되지않는다Consciousness-raising (CR) 의식 #4Consciousness-raising describes the way that learners become aware, or aremade aware, of features of the language they are learning. The term belongs290 Build-up 영어교육론 LGuideline for Pre-service Teachers a3) ᅵ!to cognitive learning theory, which claims a central role for conscious mentaloperations in learning. At the very least, it is argued learners need to noticefeatures of the input, if these features are to become intake. Of course, teacherscan highlight input features but this is no guarantee that learners will notice them.So it may be better to talk about the things that have CR potential. These include:enhancing the input to make certain items more salient; inductive learning;noticing the gap; and pushed output.의식상승이란학습자들이자신주변의언어적정보에대해주의집중하는것을 말한다. 인지주의학습이론에따르면학습자들이무한한 1064 에의단순노출에의해서는학습이일어날수없고언어자극에대해 noticings!HIS 거쳐 intakeElch 학습자들의언어적요소에의의식 ASS 높이기위한방법으로는고학습자들의주의를끌수 UTS inputB So] 제공하거나 highlight, underline SS 이용할수 있다.Constructivism 구성주의Constructivism is a theory of learning that claims that individuals activelyconstruct knowledge, rather than passively receiving it. They do this by filteringand organizing their experience so as to match their existing knowledge of theworld. If there is a mismatch between their experience and their existing mentalrepresentations, they restructure the latter to accommodate the new information.According to this view, different individuals who are exposed to the sameexperiences will each construct a different and unique reality. The view of thelearner as an individual, actively constructing personal meaning, has obviousimplication for language teaching. For a start, it suggests such passive learningprocedures as imitation and rote learning may play only a minor role. It supportsthe case for learner-centered instruction, and for learners discovering how thelanguage works for themselves. Finally, since learning is the construction ofpersonal meaning constructivism underscore the argument for personalization.A form of constructivism which emphasizes the dynamic interplay betweenindividuals and their social context is called social constructivism, and sharesmany of the principles of socio-cultural learning theory.구성주의학습이론에따르면학습자는제공되는지식을받아들이는수통적인존재가아니라스스로지식을구성하는존재 이다. 자신만의인지와경험 SS 사용하여같은지식이라할지라도개개의학습자는지식의 형태,의미는다르게형성하며때로는새로운지식을창출하기도 한다. 따라서학습의주체는학습자가되어야 하며,Appendix 01 Glossary 291Appendix교사는학생의학습을도와주는촉진 자, 정보제공자로서의역할을하게 된다. 이러한구성주의학습이론의AetO = personalization, 사회문화적학습이론등이대두하게 되었다.Content and Language Integrated Learning (CLIL) 내용언어통합 2aTeaching a subject through English, to learners whose first language is not Englishis known as content and language integrated learning (content-based teaching).CLIL belongs firmly in the tradition of the strong form of the communicativeapproach, in that there is no predetermined language syllabus. Instead,instruction is organized solely around the content. It is also closely related toimmersion teaching, whereby learners in a situation of additive bilingualism takeall or some of their school subjects in a second language. Content and languageintegrated learning instruction probably works best where teachers are adept notonly at teaching the subject matter, but also at addressing their learners’ languageneeds.내용 - 언어통합학습은 WS 교과를 SHS 가르치는내용기반교수로의사소통적접근법의 strong versionoll속한다. 내용교과를영어로가르치는 immersion, submersion 0「09191 과관련이있는데 MAKE EFL 상황에서의내용 - 기반수업 을, 후자는 ESL 상황에서의내용기반수업을 가리킨다. 내용기반수업은교과목을영어로가르치기때문에학습자들의흥미를유발하며풍부한언어적입력을제공한다는 Mola 0못하면교과내용의이해가안된다는 점, 교과내용과영어에모두능통한교사가부족하다는한계점이 있다.Context 문맥The context of a language item is its adjacent language items. In the absenceof context, it is often impossible to assign exact meaning to an item. A wordor sentence in one context can have a very different meaning in another. It issometimes necessary to distinguish between different kinds of context. On theone hand, there is the context of the accompanying text, sometimes called theco-text. Both co-text and context influence the production and interpretation oflanguage.문맥이란인접한어휘항목들간의연결로인해형성되는맥락을의미 한다. SS 이루는큰흐름이라볼수있는데하나의문맥에있는어휘는다른문맥에서는다른의미로사용될수도 있다. A comparison between a learner’s first languageand a second language would predict the errors that a learner would makelearning the latter: the greater the difference, the more likely an error. Theunderlying assumption was the behaviorist one that errors occur as a result ofinterference when the learner transfers first language habits into the second.In fact, error analyses of learners’ inter-language show that many errors thatmight be predicted on the basis of contrastive analysis do not occur. Others thatare not predicted occur. For these reasons, many errors are now attributed todevelopmental causes. That is they occur as a result of the way inter-languagedevelops naturally, irrespective of the learner’s first language. CA’s mostsuccessful predictions are in the area of phonology where the influence of thefirst language is more in evidence than it is in grammar learning.행동주의의영향으로발달한대조 EMS 모국어의간섭을오류의원인으로보고모국어와목표어의 WAS통해오류를예방하고자 하였다. There are currentlytwo schools of thought: the direct approach, and the indirect approach. Theformer argues that the characteristic features of conversation, as identified inconversation analysis, should be taught explicitly and in isolation, before beingintegrated into freer practice activities. The indirect approach, on the other hand,argues that conversation is best learned by having conversations: Accordingly,the conversation syllabus might consist of a list of topics or of situations whereconversations are likely to occur.대화는주로한사람이상이 LHe 비공식적인발화를 말한다. 명시적인대화지도를강소하는 direct approach}대화참여를통해 ete 시작, 진행, BASH] 방법을학습시켜야 SHCH= indirect approach7} 있다. 명시적인대화지도에서는알맞은주제의 선정, 대화에끼어 들기, 화제 바꾸기, 대화종결하기 SS 다룬다.00Appendix 01 Glossary 293AppendixConversation Analysis (CA) 대화분석Conversation analysis is concerned with describing the structure of conversationalinteraction, including the sequential organization of talk and the ways thatspeakers repair communication problems. CA includes turn-taking which meansavoiding either long silences or speaking at the same time when they talk, andadjacency pair, the occurrence of two consecutive turns such as a question andan answer. Other features identified by CA include conversational openings andclosing, and repair strategies.대화분석이란대화의시작부터종결까지의과정과그 PAS 분석하는 AS 말한다. 상황과문화에맞는적절한대화주제선택 하기, 상대방의발화에끼어 들기, 화제 바꾸기, 대화종결하기의전략뿐아니라상대방과의미의A협상을 Sol 원활한의사소통하기 SS 그대상으로 한다.Co-operative principle 상호협동의원리The co-operative principle is the principle that speakers try to co-operate with oneanother. When people take part in conversations they do so on the assumptionthat the other speakers will observe certain unstated “rules”. The co-operativeprinciple consists of four maxims which are quantity; make your contribution just asinformative as required, quality; make it that is true, relation; make it relevant, andmanner, avoid obscurity and ambiguity (be brief and orderly).ql0oa feam상호협동의원리는두사람이상의대화에서성공적인대화를하기위해갖추어야할대화상의 4상대방이원하는만큼의정보를 MSS quantity, 진실만을말하는 quality, 상대방의발화에관련된발화를해 0하는 relation, 상대방이알아듣기쉽게간결하고명확하게이야기하는 manner2| 원리가 있다.CorpusA corpus (plural corpora) is a collection of actually occurring texts, stores andaccessed by means of computers, and useful for investigation language use. Theuse of corpora for researching language structure and use has led to developmentof grammars and dictionaries that claim to be more reliable than their forbears,in that they are based on attested data. One way that corpus information isoften presented is in the form of a concordance (a list of words, along with eachword’s immediate context).294 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service TeachersCorous= 컴퓨터를이용하여제시되는 textafo| 언어자료를 말한다. Concordance program] corpusdlA제시하는자료중에서특정어휘의예문들을 Blot} 제시하게 된다.Correction 수정Correction is a form of feedback, when the teacher or another student providesthe correct version of an error. The amount and type of correction is closelyrelated to the teacher’s attitude to error. Where mistakes are seen as evidence ofbad habits, they need to be corrected overtly and fast. On the other hand, wheremistakes are viewed as a natural stage in the development of the learner’s inter-language, and where learners are credited with having the capacity to workthings out for themselves, teachers may use a variety of strategies to elicit peer-correction or self-correction. Second language acquisition research suggests thatlack of negative feedback may be a contributing factor to fossilization. Even ifcorrections have little direct effect on acquisition, correction may serve to remindlearners to take accuracy seriously. And attention to accuracy (also called a focuson form) is claimed to be a necessary condition for inter-language development.jo=a에」건re[것ru2aaririf내에0건{OoOWmMIN r2 >yo = Ox16 we =뜨 ftJo. Sh개aFIPCulture 문화Most definitions of culture distinguish between capital C-culture and smallc-culture. The former refers to those highly valued activities and artifacts relatedto the arts. The latter refers to the beliefs, values, traditions, and practices sharedby a particular community. It is generally recognized that language are a mixof universal concepts and of others that are more culturally specific. It is thepresence of the latter that explains why speakers of one language may perceivethe world and remember events differently from speakers of another language.A strong version of the belief that language determines thought is known asthe Sapir-Whorf hypothesis. Nowadays, the claims of linguistic determinism areAppendix 01 Glossary 295largely discredited. Otherwise, any kind of cross-cultural communication wouldbreak down constantly. And learners seem relatively adept at making conceptualadjustments when compelled to.문화는한사회의역사적 유물, 유적, 고전등과 ZS capital-CQ} 생활 양식, 가치관, 전통과관련된 small cB구분 한다. 언어습득과관련된문화지도는주로 smali-cB 대상으로 한다. 현재의관점에서는언어도문화의한부분으로타문화권의화자와의성공적인의사소통을위해서는문화적인영향도고려해야하기때문에 naan문화지도가중요 하다. 문화와언어간의관련성에대한 71S strong versionz} weak versionO| 있는데전자는언어의절대성 을, 후자는언어의상대성을주장하고있다Dialogue 대화In the language classroom, a dialogue is either the text of a two-way spokenexchange, or it is the activity of having such an exchange. Dialogues have alwaysbeen a popular means for presenting and practicing language, one reason beingthat dialogue is the most common and most widespread way that language isused in real life.=나얼진행된 다. “ine 가장일반적인의사소통의방식이며실제언어사용의 ASS 가능하게한다Direct method 직접교수법This is an umbrella term for a wide range of language teaching methods thatemerged in the later part of the nineteenth century. They shared the belief thatonly the target language should be used in the classroom, and that thereforetranslation should be avoided at all costs. Instead of translation, form-meaningassociations should be established using real objects, pictures, or demonstration.The teacher’s role was to maintain an extended “conversation” with the learners.The direct method was a response to the growing demand for learning languages,and offered a refreshing alternative to the bookish grammar-translation methodthat prevailed at the time. In the USA, the direct method ingested behavioristtheory and metamorphosed into audiolingualism. In the UL and Europe it becamethe situational approach, but its core principle, the exclusive use of the targetlanguage, survives as an article of faith amongst many teachers to this day.296 ~~ Build-up 영어교육론 1AEGuideline for Pre-service Teachers 23)문법번역식교수법에대한반발로등장한교수법으로모국어가아닌목표어로지도하는특징이는철저히배제되며보다명확한이해를위해실물 교재, 그림등을이용하여| 르치되문법은 Holes 통해 7 남적으로제시된 다. 교사의 시범, 질문과학생의대답과Discourse, Discourse analysis 담화분석Discourse is any connected piece of speaking or writing. Discourse analysis isprincipally the study of how such stretches of language achieve both cohesionand coherence. Whereas traditional grammar is concerned only with sentencesand their components, discourse analysis seeks to identify patterns andregularities of language “beyond the sentence”. It is closely related to, and partlyoverlaps with, other textbased fields of study, including conversation analysis.For the language teacher, the main implications of discourse analysis are inthe teaching of writing, especially with regard to the ways that texts are madecohesive.AoJz담화분석은문장과문장사이에존재하는관련성과응집력을분석 한다. 같은문장이더라도저로다른로다른의미로사용되기때문에 sentence level 이상, B 문장과문장간의연결에서발생하는연상 , 즉서로구하는 것이다. 담화분석은대화분석을포괄하여사용되기도 한다.Discourse marker 담희표시어Discourse markers (also called pragmatic markers) are words or expressionslike well, anyway, mean, actually, that normally come at the beginning of anutterance, and function to orient the listener to what will follow. They do thiseither by indicating some kind of change of direction in the talk, or by appealingto the listener in some way. Linkers such as but, and, so, because, which connectwhat has been said to what follows, are sometimes classified as discourse markersas well.담화표시어란문장앞에위치하면서다음의발화의 WSS 예측하게끔하는 단어, 구를 말한다. 예를들어 64 은발화자가앞서얘기하던내용과반대되는말을하고자함을 나타내고, | meanS 자신이한 BS 보충설명 6것을예측할수 있다. 적절한담화표시자의사용은상다방의담화를이해하는데도움이될뿐만아니라 x바=하는데 SSS 준다.0브Pa0ratmebe뻔Appendix 01 Glossary 297AppendixDisplay questionDisplay questions are questions asked by teachers in order that learners can“display” their knowledge. They typically initiate classroom interaction, and iscalled an IRF (interaction—-response—follow up) sequence. In language classrooms,display questions are usually aimed at finding out what learners can say inthe target language. Display questions contrast with real questions (also calledreferential questions) which are motivated by the need to find out somethingthat the person asking the question doesn’t know. Some researchers suggest thatboth the quality and quantity of communication in the classroom improves whenteachers ask more real questions than display questions.Display question2 교사가자신도알고있는정답을학생으로부터이끌어내기위해학생에게하는이와 HICH® referential 046600「 은교사도모르는답을학생으로부터이끌어내기위해하는질문으로주로구드=학생과관련된질문이대부분 이다. display questions 주로학생들이수업내용을이해하고 있는지, 영어의수준이어느정도인지파악을하기위해실시하는경우가많으며교사의 AES 학생들의발화와의사소통을촉진하는수단으로많이사용된 다. Drills that are targeted at enticed structuresare sometimes called pattern practice drills. Drills follow a prompt-responsesequence, where the prompt usually comes from the teacher, and the studentsrespond, either in chorus (a choral drill) or individually. A substitution drillrequires the students to substitute one element of the pattern with the prompt,making any necessary adjustment. A variable substitution drill is the same,but the prompts are not restricted to one element of the pattern. Drills weredefining feature of the audiolingual method, and were designed to reinforcegood language ‘habits’. With the demise of audiolingualism, drilling fell fromfavor. However, many teachers—even those who subscribe to a communicativeapproach—feel the need for some form of repetition practice of the kind thatdrills provide. This may be for the purpose of developing accuracy, or as a formof fluency training. Hence communicative drills were developed communicative298 Build-up 영어교육론 lGuideline for Pre-service Teachers S3) ᅵdrill is still essentially repetitive, and focuses on a particular structure or pattern,but it has an information gap element built.ps보osDrill활동은일정한패턴의 단어, 구 , SYS 교사의 AlHol 따라반복적으로연습하는 BSS 말한다.은일반적으로교사의발화를그대로따라하기도하지만교사가 006 를제공하면학생들이해당하는분만바꾸어발화하는 64606044007 drill, 두단어이상을대치하여연습하는 multiple substitution drill, 대치하는어요소가바뀌는 moving 희아 substitution drill 등이 있다. 반복동이며행동주의의쇠퇴와함께그중요성은보다약해졌지만특정 어휘, 표현의도움이되기때문에현재까지도널리사용되고있는활동 이다.1 yoIfelreoeflmc 0+net [ 오 4ko roEllipsis #2Ellipsis is the leaving out of elements of a sentence because they are eitherunnecessary or because their sense can be worked out from the immediatecontext. Ellipsis is very common in spoken language. Ellipsis of function words isalso a common feature of certain text types.에생략은 164 에서불필요하거나예측가능한 BAS 생략하는것을 말한다. 주로구어에서많이사용 된다.iError 오류An error is an instance of the learner’s language that dos not conform to acceptednorms of usage, and which is attributed to incomplete or faulty learning. Errorsare sometimes distinguished from mistakes, the former being due to lackof knowledge, and the latter being due to the demands of performance. Inprinciple, the test of a mistake is whether the learner can self-correct effortlessly.Errors can be categorized in a number of ways: an omission where an obligatoryelement is left out, an addition where an element has been added unnecessarily,a misselection error where the wrong item has been used, a misformationwhere wrong form of the right word, and misordering error when sentencecomponents are in the wrong order. Errors are also classified according to theirpossible cause. This is the particular concern of error analysis. Transfer errors arethose that result from the influence of the learner’s first language. On the otherhand, developmental errors are those that occur as a natural part of the learningprocess. It used to be thought that all errors were transfer errors what were calledAppendix 01 Glossary 299Appendixinterference. Research has shown, however, that there are certain errors that alllearners appear to make regardless of their first language, and in a predictablechronological order. Many of these are due to the overgeneralization of a rule.오류는학생들의발화에서부정확한표현이며행동주의에서는 CHES 잘못된것으로보았으나현재의관점에서는오류도학습자의중간언어발달의한과정으로긍정적으로보고 있다. 교사의오류수정의정도는어느오류에대해, 어느정도로수정을하느냐가주요문제인데오류수정의정도는수업목표에따라달라져야 한다. 정확성에AAS 둔수업이라면오류수정은 global errort# 아니라 local 하아도수정의대상으로하여학습자의발화가끝난후실시를하는것이바람직하며유창성과의사소통에초점을둔수업이라면전체적인의미에영향을주는global 6 아만을대상으로하여학습자의활동이끝난후 |!0*/-40 treatmentOl|A| 전체교실활동으로실시해야한다.Experiential learning 22 중심교수법Experiential learning is a general term for “deep-end” approaches to learning thatrate direct practical experience over the learning and application of abstract rules.In language learning terms, this might take the form of task-based learning, ofdiscovery-learning, or of content-based learning. Experiential language learningshares with mentalist theories of learning a belief in the value of learners activelyworking things out for themselves. It also shares with humanism a commitment towhole-person learning, and, with critical pedagogy, a belief in the transformativepower of direct experience rather than simply applying knowledge that has been“handed down” by some higher authority.경험중심교수법은 - 교사의명시적인지식의전달이아닌학습자스스로가 AHS 통해새로운 USS 학습하는것을 말한다. Experiential learning2 언어를총체적으로|=접근하며좌되와 PS 모두활용하기때문에보다효과적인학습이가능하며학습자의동기를높여 준다.Facilitation 히습의촉진To facilitate a process, such as language learning, is to help make it happen.Facilitation is a way of thinking about teaching that recognizes the fact thatteachers do not directly cause learning, but that they can provide the conditionsin which learning happens. The teacher facilitates the process by managing the300 Build-up 영어교육론 1Guideline for Pre-service Teacherslearning situation, the role of facilitator, therefore, involves not just knowledgeof teaching techniques and subject matter knowledge, but interpersonal skills aswell. A good example of the “teacher-as-facilitator” is in community languagelearning, where the teacher’s role is primarily that of a consultant, providinglearner with the language they need to construct their own conversations.Feedback 피드백 ( 교정적 정보)Feedback is the information, either immediate or delayed, that learners get ontheir performance. At least some of this feedback may have a long-term effecton their knowledge of the language. Traditionally, feedback takes the form ofcorrection. Correction is called negative feedback: it is a clear message that thelearner has produced an error. But feedback can also be positive. Feedback canbe explicit or it can be implicit since the teacher does not overtly indicate thatthe learner has made an error. Researchers into second language acquisition arein two minds, however. If the learners’ errors elicit only positive feedback, andtherefore go unnoticed and uncorrected, these errors may become fossilized.Other researchers, however, have argued that even explicit negative feedbackhas no long-term effect either. This is because the learner’s developing mentalgrammar is not yet “ready” for the correction. To counter this argument,supporters of negative feedback argue that, while the effect of correction mightnot be either immediate or predictable, constant “nagging” serves to remindlearners to pay attention to form. And paying attention to form is good for themin the long run.교실내의피드백은학습자의발화와언어수행에대해교사가관련된정보를제공하는것으로긍정적인피드백중성적인 피드백, 부정적인피드백으로나 된다. 또한정의적인피드백과인지적인피드백이있는데학습자의정의적인 SHS 강화시키기위해서정의적인피드백은긍정적인측면에서만 MSS 해야 한다. 인지적인피드백에오류가있을경우부정적인피드백을제공하여 OFS 처리해야하는데유창성이수업목표인경우에는= oOglobal errorO|| 한해서, 정확성이 SHO] BL local 아까지도그대상으로 한다. Fluency is primarily the ability to produceand maintain speech in real time. Classroom activities that target fluency need toprepare the learner for real-time speech production. Learning and memorizinglexical chunks, including useful conversational gambits, is one approach.Drills may help here, as will some types of communicative activity that involverepetition. Some interactive and competitive language games have this effect.Drama activities, such as role-plays, recreate conditions of real-time languageuse, and are therefore good for developing fluency. Finally, learners can achievegreater fluency from learning a repertoire of communication strategies.Formulaic languageFormulaic language refers to those sequences of two or more words that operateas a single unit. This means they are stored in the memory, and retrieved, as ifthey were one-word vocabulary items. Also called Cexical) chunks, multi-wordunits, readymades, prefabricated language and holophrases, formulaic languagecan be classified into collocations, phrasal verbs, idioms, and discourse markers.Formulaic language= 하나의단어처럼함께쓰이는정형화된 BAS 말한다. There are various theories as to what causes fossilization. It hasbeen hypothesized that the lack of instruction, specially the lack of a focus onform, is the main cause. This is used as an argument for giving explicit attentionto grammar. Another theory is that fossilization may be due to the lack ofnegative feedback on errors, a view that is used to justify correction. Fossilizationmay also be due to the fact that learners have not been “pushed” to make theiroutput more accurate.“kJ화석화의원인은명시적인문법 지도, 오류에대한부정적인 피드백, 상호작용속의 pushed output) 부재등이(해^Function 기능The function of a language item is its communicative purpose. Language is morethan simply forms and their associated meanings. It is also the communicativeuses to which there forms and meanings are put. There is no one-to-one matchbetween form and function. Assigning a function to a text or an utterance usuallyrequires knowledge of the context in which the text is used.언어의기능은의사소통에 있다. 의사소통은상호간의의미전달에의해이루어지는것인데성공적인의사소통을위해서는담화내에서의의미파악이중요 하다.Functional syllabus 기능중심교수요목A functional syllabus is a syllabus based around a list of language functions suchas asking for information; making request; greeting people. Functional syllabuseswere first developed to support a communicative approach. In contrast to theprevailing structural syllabuses of the time, they were meaning based rather thanAppendix 01 Glossary 30301 Glossaryform based. They were often combined with language notions to form what wascalled a functional-notional syllabus.기능중심교수요목은인지주의학습이론에서지나치게언어의형태에초점을둔것에반하여언어의본질적인목적인두고이러한기능을교수요목으로설정한것에서시작 되었다. 기능중심부탁하기등의기능들로이루어져 있다.Function word 기능어Function words, also called grammar words, are those words which have amainly grammatical function. They contrast with content words, which carrythe main informational load. Function words are auxiliary verb, determiners,pronouns, preposition, conjunctions, and adverbs.기능어는내용어와는반대로단어가지니는의미가없거나문장에서 See 의미를지니지못하는 HOSS =문법적인기능을담당하고 있다. 구어에서는흔히강세를 Bl Ot 발음이되지않거나축약된형태로도많이사용 된다.Grammar-translation method 문법번역식교수법Grammar translation is a language teaching method that developed out of theway that classical languages such as Latin and Greek were traditionally taught.The grammar part comes from the fact that grammar is taught deductively andthat grammatical accuracy is highly prioritized. Grammar-translation was seriouslychallenged by the advent of the direct method. Thus, inductive presentationswould replace deductive ones, whole texts would replace isolated sentences, andthere would be a focus not only on reading and writing but also on speaking andlistening.고전어를가르치던교수법에서유래한문법번역식교수법은학습의주요 USS 문법지도와모국어로의번역을0 oO대상으로 한다. 언어형태가연역적인방법으로먼저제시되고정확성을수업의 SHE 하는데이에대한반발로교수304 = Build-up 영어교육론 1uideline for Pre-service TeachersGroupwork 그룹활동Groupwork is a form of classroom interaction where learners work together,part of all of the time, in small groups. The best size for a group is probablyfrom three to five learners: anything larger may mean that not all learners willcontribute often or equally. Groupwork works best if there is a clear outcome tothe task, such as making a decision, performing to the rest of the class. It can bea good idea to assign roles to individual members, and also important that theseating arrangement permits all the members of the group to see and hear oneanother. Finally, the teacher needs to monitor groupwork to ensure that learnersare on-task, to be available to answer questions, and to provide feedbackCincluding correction) on task performance.그룹활동은학생들간의상호작용을도모하는가장흔한교실활동중의 하나이다. 하나의그룹에는 4~6 명 ,적당한데그이유는학생들에게적절한발언의기회가부여되며특정학생에게역할이집중되지않는oOImmersion 몰입프로그램An immersion program is one in which children are taught some or all of theirschool subjects in a language that is not their mother tongue. It is aimed atfostering bilingualism. Immersion should be distinguished from submersion,which is what happens when individuals who speak one language are placedin a situation in which their education is mediated using another. In general,immersion education is not prejudicial, either to the ongoing development of thepupils’ first language, or to their overall academic performance. Moreover, theyachieve a near-native level of understanding of the second language, although, inproduction, their grammatical accuracy falls short of native speakers.교과내용을 SHS 가르치는몰입프로그램은이중병행사용을 SACS 한다. The key factors are often grouped into biological factorssuch as age and gender; personality factors such as confidence and self-esteem;cognitive factors such as aptitude, learning style and memory; and affectivefactors such as motivation and anxiety. One of the outcomes of this researchhas been the development of learner training procedures, which target thosefactors that are susceptible to change and improvement. These include thelearner’s use of learning strategies, or techniques of improving memory. Anotherway of responding to the fact that learners are all different has been in theindividualization of learning, through, for example, one-to-one teaching, and theuse of self-access centers.Information exchanging 점보의교환Exchanging information is one of the key functions of language. Language that isused in this way is called transactional language. It is typically performed by theasking of questions and by answering with statements. Teaching learners how toask for and give information is a core component of most syllabuses, tight fromthe outset. Popular activities for practicing this function include dialogues andinformation gap activities.정보의교환은대인관계의유지를목적으로 SHE interpersonal language2h= 달리특정있다. 정보교환의연습활동은대화나정보격차활동을통해 이루어진다.Input 일력Input is the spoken or written language that learners are exposed to. You cannot learn a language without input. In his input hypothesis, the linguist StephenKrashen argues that input is all that is necessary for language acquisition to take306 Build-up SolwS= 1Guideline for Pre-service Teachersplace. But the input must be comprehensible, and it must contain grammaticalforms that are one step more advanced than the current state of the learners’interlanguage. The modifications such as simplified, delivered at a slower paceand more elaborated input may assist interlanguage development. Michael Long,argues that input is most effective when it has been made comprehensiblethrough negotiation of meaning.인지주의이론에 따르면. inputS intaked}7| 위해서는의식적인 noticingO| 필수적 이다.
